this world and the Hereafter. As if He had said about Allah, glorified and exalted be He: "We — every thing We have created according to a measure" (1) of the matter of the two worships in knowledge and deed, which the community needs in its religion and its worldly life. "We have measured it" — meaning, we have brought it from revelation and Shari'ah in measured form; that is, we have made it in her power so that she may come out, in interpretation, to what she deserves.

Section Thirteen of Chapter Eight

The author of al-Islah said:

Qada' is the posterior act, since it has been established on one side that what comes out to action comes out of the natural world with its support, and is done by it, and from its side it attains completeness. Therefore, qada' became the same as the speaker, because he went out to action and obtained perfection with its support and aid.

Section Fourteen of Chapter Eight

He said: (2)

That all the essences were emanated from the prior — there is a contradiction, because the posterior is what (3) is emanated from the prior, and not by way of predestination; rather, what is meant by saying it is that the emanation from which the physical world was determined to be something of it, in accordance with what we have explained in the chapter of qadar, not the posterior.

Section Fifteen of Chapter Eight

The author of al-Nusra said:

In a chapter in which "We have created it," He intends the image of the two worlds from among them, and the measure of

what He intends by the posterior is the stabilization of the matter, in which all the spiritual and physical images appeared from among them — for it is not the case that the existence of things bodily was and was not according to his body, as he reminded us of the corruption of what we have shown in the foundation upon which his words are based. And were it not that to discuss what the existence of the essences entailed upon the first is outside the limit of writing, we would bring it; and it will not be mentioned in *al-Qur'an*, Allah willing, and we have written it.

Section Sixteen of Chapter Eight

The author of al-Islah said:

As for the interpretation of the words of the Messenger of Allah, *"Flee from Allah's qada' to His qadar,"* rather, he wanted to flee from the latter of the prior endorsement to the posterior statement, like the flight of a man from the fire — which is the proof of the endorsement — to the water, which is the proof of the statement. He wanted to flee from the thing that had been sealed and decreed, lest he be prepared, pushing him toward what he had not yet undergone — that is to say, while he is irregular.

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) passed from Allah's qada' to His qadar because of a cause, and the cause was the leaning wall that he warned against falling, and he hastened his walking, and he said: he wanted to strike a parable for them, and the wall — an inclined one is a building that has tended to fall, and it is on the border that some of them may have something of apostasy and hypocrisy, and he has inclined to debauchery from obedience; because if he apostatized, he fell from his rank. As Allah says: *"And they found in it a wall on the verge of collapse, so he set it up"* (Quran 18:77). I mean: one of the limits was concerned with hypocrisy and apostasy, so he set him up, so that he was fixed and did not topple, nor did he fall — as did the leaning wall that the Messenger of Allah (peace) hastened to walk past. He had known a limit upon whom he felt

1 — Fell in copy (A).

- 164


<!-- page 167 -->
hypocrisy, and he tended to repudiate it, so he set it upright. The "setting upright" denotes the speed of walking, because following him in walking signifies the statement, the proof, the hurry, and the speed of walking.

He used to address those given to hypocrisy with preaching and warning — in the outward form without the inward statement (and the decree on the outward, as we have explained, and the elimination of the inward) — and his flight from Allah's decree to His destiny was for the sake of this wall, careful that it not fall (careful of itself, that it not flee from the dignity with which Allah Almighty has honored him, which is the degree to which Allah has elevated him).

The author of al-Nusrah said:

It is to multiply, be careful.

It is not a matter of interpreting "flee from Allah's decree to His destiny" according to what one imagines — the owner of the Islah, namely that he was (3) fleeing from the next rank to the preceding rank — because the prophets, peace be upon them, never ask for heights, and asking for heights is not asking for...

But we would say, with the help of Allah Almighty and His blessings, that the meaning herein divides into three meanings, and each of these proves that the elimination is of the preceding and the predestining is of the next. One of them — the greatest, the most accurate in meaning — is that what is meant by him is his flight from Allah's decree to His destiny, that the preceding, God willing, is the support, and the next is the composition. And who the speaker is, is the authorship of the Shariah, and it is the basic interpretation of everyone — the interpretation that is.

The end is more like an endorsement, and the composition is more like a synthesis, so the speaker (peace be upon him) was, in saying this, showing that it is similar in the composition of the laws and therefore in the structure of the world. He is not like the preceding one; he fled from the decree of Allah, which is the preceding, and he did not...

He likens it from the aspect that is the creation of support to its destiny, which is interpretation. He likened himself to him.

And the second meaning is his nation's media, that he benefits from the first by means of the second, so he was, in everything he wanted to stand upon from the first, by means of the second referring to him — as if he said, "Return to all that I want to understand." It is the reason between me and the intellect, and it is the second. This is the second meaning.

And the third meaning, the most honorable, is what the author of the book has mentioned, peace be upon him: namely, his escape from the intensity of the light of the support of the preceding to the support of the next, as the grandfather was with his spiritual power and could not bear it until his identity almost faded. This is what he said in the story of Moses (peace be upon him).

We say:

As for the owner of the Islah, he moved in the interpretation of the verse in a way identical to what the matter is in the sense of decree and destiny, and it is good — even if he said it, it would not have been the Prophet (peace be upon him), a prophet who responds to the unseen from the universes (2) and events.

In the pronouns of what Allah Almighty had singled out for him of the Revelation, he wanted to clarify how he used to open up to him what was being thrown at him seriously, and he said: "Go back," and he said, "Flee from me." I seriously cross the limits of Allah Almighty by a number of events that are almost — and the universes, which is the judgment of Allah, which inevitably goes out into action to His destiny, which is the creation of Allah Almighty of the souls and horizons and their movements that indicate what His ability in them is, to open up to me what was between us in the door of revelation.

And therefore Allah says: "We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in their own selves until it becomes clear to them that it is" — and "Those who contemplate the creation of the heavens and the earth say: Our Lord, You have not created this in vain" — does not indicate that his existence has been preceded and that his existence has been delayed from the universes.

Rather, he signifies it and pronounces it, as if he said, "Go back to me," and he will be seriously thrown into me. The book (Rest of the Mind) includes an explanation of that.

Chapter Seventeen of Chapter Eight

As for the owner of al-Nasra, his behavior in the answer that he gave is proof of his submission to the author of the Islah, since he did not mention anything that would oppose the author of the Islah in what he based his words on, nor what he said — except the meanings he counted first; and he mentioned that each of them proves the elimination of the preceding and the predestining of the next.

It is not because the speaker is similar in his composition of the Shari'ah, as he has said, in order that he return in all that he wanted (1) to realize the next — as he has proved and obliges him. To him that proves that the elimination is of the preceding and the predestining is of the next, there is no occasion between the elimination of the preceding and the meanings that he has already expressed, even if the meaning of decree and destiny is identical.

As the case is with the first and the second, and it is appropriate for them from one side, it may be said that the decree and the predestination are upon them from that side. But the decree means what has been said above, and so is destiny — and it is not worth saying about the first and the second that they are two of the things that are obligatory for their meaning. Whoever says about them is as if he had said about honey, which is naturally sweet, that it is patience that is naturally bitter.

Chapter Eighteen of Chapter Eight

As for his analogy in the second meaning of the speaker, it does not correspond to what it is.

<!-- page 170 -->
The law of the guiding call, because the speaker is in the world of the body, and the world of religion is the place of the preceding one, and the place of the guardian in them is the next place in the world of creativity. So the speaker and the foundation are two parables for the preceding and the next, and two parables for the sun and the moon.

Chapter Nineteen of Title VIII

As for the third meaning that he mentioned positively, that the speaker fled from the intensity of the light of the preceding support to the support of the next — which is contrary to the duty and interpretation in the case of the grandfather that was cited — it needs to be investigated, and the words of the author of the Islah in the chapter come stronger.

Chapter Twenty of Chapter Eight

The author of the Islah (1) said, quoting from the verse in the story of Moses (peace be upon him): "My Lord, show me, that I may look upon You." He said, "You will not see Me, but look at the mountain; if it settles in its place, you will see Me." And when his Lord appeared to the mountain, He made it Dhaka (crumbled to dust).

He was told: "You will not see Me, but look" — and he knew that he would not attain it, and he ordered him to limit himself to what was occurring to him seriously. And he knew that the one who asked him could not be like him with his kindness — how can he get what he does not see?

He says:

"If it settles in its place, you will see Me," and when his Lord appeared to the mountain, He made it Dhaka. "And Moses fell down struck by a thunderbolt." When he learned that he had sinned in asking for what he could not receive, he prayed to me — (1) Dropped in copy (A). (2) The sentence is completely omitted in copy (1).
- 168-0

<!-- page 171 -->
When his Lord woke him, he said, "Glory be to You, I repent to You."

Sahib al-Nusrah said:

"My Lord, show me, that I may look upon You" — "He said, you will not see Me" — meaning, you cannot bear, and you cannot be patient upon that rank. "But look at the mountain" — and he is the grandfather, with his closeness to me. "Settle on his rank" that I have given him, and bear what I have shown him — I will bear it for you. But the grandfather did not bear that, because it was manifested to him, and his identity nearly... This is what he said.

We say:

The interpretation of this verse, according to what each of the two persons used to say, did not place Moses (peace be upon him) as the highest of the prophets; rather, it preserves the upper limits. They took him out of the group of scholars and counted him among the ignorant, by claiming that he asked for what he does not perceive from above him among the borders. How could this be, when the matter passes upon him in it? The interpretation of the verse is different from what he said, because it was not addressed to him.

Moses (peace be upon him) was with the upper borders, but he was addressing him with the borders when he had not yet reached the rank of pronunciation. He asked the author of the command, before his time had come — because he was in the time of a period of intermission, and the people of truth were under affliction, the covering, and concealment from the side of opposites and violators. And Moses, peace be upon him, saw in himself a power that he reckoned he could use in his time, if he commanded the lifting of that ordeal from the people of truth, and taking revenge upon the enemies of Allah, and the politics of the nation by the policy of truth — as the foundation, peace be upon him, estimated by the power he found in himself.

What he appreciated and repented of, when he knew that he had sinned, the sun returned to him, and answered what we have explained in our letters by interpretation. So Moses (peace be upon him) asked the author of the matter, namely Shu'ayb, when he came to him and he was his Lord, after he had explained to him his command in the matter. He found in himself the strength and ability for politics — which is when he said: "O Lord, show me, that I may look upon You" — meaning, command me, that I may manage this matter and reveal the grief.
- 169

<!-- page 172 -->
"You will not see Me" means: you will not see Me do any of that, nor will those in this time. For everything has its time and season, and this is not its time — taking these means away from the umma from what they follow of their whims. There is no time to reply to things down to the laws of politics; and (1) what we say to you is not done. Shu'ayb replied to him, peace be upon him, to alert him to his mistake in his request in the best of ways, and to teach him that what he asked for is difficult, and in his time it is not done by those who have the power, help, and equipment. How then could it be on the side of a great man who is in the da'wah, a man of great worldly presidency, who has the help, the wealth, the men, and the kingdom?

He said to Moses, peace be upon him: I have learned that this matter is not done in this time, and it is difficult and cannot be measured. It is not that I refrain stingily towards you, nor altruistically to delay you from your station — but look to the mountain, meaning this man who has worldly power, equipment, and capability. "If it settles in its place, you will see Me" — that is, if he is fixed in what he has been commanded, and is enabled, by his power and help, to lay out the provisions of the policy of truth — and it was said to him: "You will see Me do what I have asked of them." I mean: when he ordered him to erect a beacon of truth, He made it Dhaka — that is, the matter narrowed upon the people, they did not accept the command, they split the staff, and the matter was confused and disturbed.

His presidency was about to vanish, when the people went out against him. And Moses learned, peace be upon him, then, that what he was destined to accomplish at that time was destined to be impossible. The owner of the matter, who is his Lord, knew the story better than him, so he was awakened — he was bewildered by that warning, and he said: "Glory be to Almighty Allah, I repent to You." So he retracted his statement, regretted, and was patient with what the owner of al-Nusrah had ordered him to do.

When that period in which he had hired him had elapsed, then the time came, and there came something of which he was right. And he said: "You will see Me" — surrender the matter, and do what you want — for this is an interpretation.

(1) It fell in copy (A).
(2) The term is stated in copy (1).
- 170

<!-- page 173 -->
The verse — not what is appreciated by the one who puts down and raises up, and does not match.

Chapter Twenty-One of Title VIII

The author of al-Nusrah said:

As for his protest by saying, "And the creation of everything according to the measure of estimation, this is clearer evidence that destiny belongs to the next, and decree is the moral over the preceding" — the meaning of his saying "and the creation of everything" that the preceding one wanted to do is because the mind is all things, and all things are the mind.

And we say:

The words of decree and destiny may have preceded, so show by them that decree and destiny — it is not permissible to say about the preceding (1) and the next, nor what is meant by the Almighty's saying "and the creation of all things that He lost in estimation," except what the owner of al-Nusrah went to. We have already shown its corruption, and that he is not worthy of the preceding or therefore of the next, to be called decree and destiny.

Rather, what is meant by "He created everything" is that He created everything, because He made everything — with regard to the matter of religion and interests, outwardly or inwardly, by the power of revelation and Shariah. He estimated it, in the appreciation of what the revelation and the Shari'ah have to do with all the sciences, which have to do with religion and interests, and they are in them by force and interpretation, which brings them out of them.

Chapter Twenty-Two of Chapter Eight

As for saying that the mind is all things, and all things are the mind, this is a matter that is not true. The physical world, with all it gathers, is not a mind; it is a thing. And better than what is attributed to it is the meaning of saying that the mind is all things, and all things —

(1) It fell in copy (b).
- 171


<!-- page 174 -->
It is the intellect, because the intellect — which is identical with the command of Allah — is the cause of the existence of all things, physical and non-physical alike; and the existence of all things proceeds from the intellect and toward its purpose.

Chapter Twenty-Three of Title Eight

The author of al-Nusrah said:
Allah has permitted the Prophets the inner meanings of the laws and has dispensed with their literal use in His saying: "There is no blame upon those who believe and do righteous deeds for what they have eaten, so long as they fear Allah and believe and do righteous deeds; then fear Him and believe; then fear Him and do good — and Allah loves the doers of good."

We say:
The verse contains no mention of permission for the prophets to abandon the canons of the Shari'ah. I do not know how he reached this conclusion before the saying had been properly examined. The interpretation of this verse is other than what he has claimed. Allah Almighty knew that souls do not attain happiness, do not reach the degree of perfection, and do not pass from the limit of potency to the limit of act except through work and knowledge — both of which require every human being to perform the two acts of worship, in knowledge and in deed, so that they may attain happiness in the two abodes. And since souls cannot attain perfection and happiness except through these two acts of worship, then whichever soul abandons both of them, or even one of them, is far from attaining perfection. This consequence remains with the soul so long as it is alive — held to account between His hands — until the time of its transfer: either to Paradise, if it kept the two, or to the Fire, if it abandoned them or one of them, until Allah forgives it, as we have explained in our books. And beyond what has been said above, the work of the souls and the reformation of morals is the greatest jihad,
- 172-0

<!-- page 175 -->
as the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) said: "and the acquisition of virtues" — by way of spiritual discipline and knowledge, in relation to what lies above it, as the call itself requires. If the state of souls in worship is according to this analogy, then how is it permissible to grant license to oneself or to anyone else — to dispense with the limits and abandon the work and the perfection of souls that come from them — and what becomes deficient in them? No: the verse has an interpretation other than the first, with a particular bearing on those who summon the preachers to the Tawhid of Allah Almighty and to the knowledge of His limits through the Imams (peace be upon them).

The Speaker (peace be upon him), knowing that his community would differ after him and that each group would cling to its own — some speaking of a doctrine according to their own opinions, their deficient minds, and their preferences forced upon the community of guidance (the prayers of Allah be upon those for whom Allah has not made any light) — knowing also that the preachers would suffer from the various nations every severity in their resistance to them and in their challenge to those doctrines, granted in his loyal Imams (peace and blessings of Allah be upon them) licenses for the preachers of the da'wa to consider sciences not of their own creed, on conditions. He said: "There is no blame upon those who believe and do righteous deeds for what they have eaten, so long as they fear Allah and believe and do righteous deeds." Meaning: those who call to the Tawhid of Allah and to the knowledge of His limits on behalf of the deputies (peace be upon them) — those who believe the respondents when they call to the rope of Allah, who hold fast to their wilayah, who are free of doubts and suspicions concerning the religion of Allah, and who have reached a degree of perfection and connection — bear no blame, that is, no constraint, in what they have eaten, that is, in what they study from sciences that are not of their own creed, so that those sciences become like a weapon with which they fight opponents in proving the truth — provided they fear and believe and do righteous deeds. That is one condition: namely, that their path is straight in obedience to Allah Almighty by following His Messenger,
(1) Fell in copy (a).
(2) Fell in copy (b).
- 173

<!-- page 176 -->
in belief in His limits, and in the establishment of both acts of worship in accordance with what He says. "Then fear and believe" — this is a second condition (1), meaning: obey the Messenger in what he commands, and the one in charge after him in his place, and call to them outwardly and inwardly. "Then fear and do good" — this is a third condition, meaning: obey the Imam in the one whom he establishes as a deputy, and do well in calling to the Tawhid of Allah under his leadership. If they do this and observe these conditions, then there is no harm for them in considering those doctrines and sciences that belong to other peoples, and there is no narrowing of their religion in doing so; rather, those sciences help them with what they need in resisting the enemies, and assist whoever seeks reassurance regarding the limits. This is the interpretation of the verse, and it contains no permission to abandon the use of the Shari'ah; rather, it is a license to consider the sciences on the conditions mentioned above. And the verdict on every interpretation that leads to permitting what Allah has forbidden, or to forbidding what He has permitted, or to altering the ranks of the limits of Allah Almighty — making light of the Shari'ah and the rites of the Hanifi religion, calling for abandoning work in it and acquiring happiness by refusing to do so — is that it is a corrupt interpretation. Our loyal Imams (peace be upon them from Allah Almighty) are pure of what he has said, and of every interpretation that contradicts what the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions said.

Chapter Twenty-Four of Title VIII

The author of al-Nusrah said:
The decree (qada) is the beginning, the apportioning (qadar) is the middle, and completion is the end — because apportioning can only proceed by the decree.
(1) In copy (b) what came in it.
(2) In copy (1) the full.
- 174

<!-- page 177 -->
Then he said:
If the decree is the end, it is not right to call it a decree, because the decree comes before all else, and things come after the decree, and the decree is for a thing. Perfection is not for nothing; rather, perfection is for the very thing that becomes perfect.

We say:
In all that has gone before in his words, the answer is bound up with fate and destiny — enough has been said to comprehend his words and to extend the discussion — without going beyond what we had intended.
- 175

<!-- page 178 -->
Chapter Nine of the Book of Riyadh
On Ruling Between the Two
(He spoke about it in the chapter of the Law of Adam and the wilayah of Noah, peace be upon him.)

Chapter One

The author of al-Islah said:
Whoever claims that the beginning of the speaker-prophets (peace be upon them) had no Shari'ah is mistaken. He is also mistaken when he counts them among those who are "determined" (mutimmun), according to what we have explained, because determination occurs only by copying the Shari'ah or by renewing it — and the first Pronouncer had no Shari'ah preceding him to abrogate, so the name of determination does not apply to him as we have presented. He was the first to draw the lines of religion in command and prohibition. And whoever works to benefit from what the rest of the speaker-prophets drew in their apparent laws — what is inferred from the subtleties (the recommended meanings of the parables, called interpretation, which is the manifestation of the words of the wise) — knows that every drawing pronounced (peace be upon them), every command, prohibition, and act of servitude, is a law: small or great, few or many. Each speaker has only as much as he is commanded, and he does not exceed it. Some of them
- 176

<!-- page 179 -->
had many statutes, and some were restricted to a little and limited in the drawing of the laws — as we see that fasting in the Law of Moses (peace be upon him) is less than what it is in the Law of Jesus (peace be upon him); or, in the Law of Jesus there is more than what is in the Law of Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him); and likewise other rulings in religion vary according to the difference (1) of their cycles and the measure of what they were commanded.

And no one should think that this great cycle — the longest of these cycles — passed without work, that its people lived without benefit, and that there were no apparent statutes drawn out in its rulings. For if there were no work, no benefit, no statutes, no interpretation, no inwardness, and no real summons, then everything collapses: the da'wa rests on the Shari'ah; interpretation requires the revelation; the inner requires the outer; the meaning requires the parable. If there is no outer, then there is no inner, no call, and no Shari'ah; creation is neglected and the people are left in ignorance — for knowledge is paired with work, which is the origin of wisdom among the wise, as they have said: "Wisdom is action with knowledge." It is impossible to say that the people of that cycle were in such a state.

Rather, we say:
The first Pronouncer required the name of "speaker" in order to compose a Shari'ah; otherwise he would not have been counted among the six Pronouncers, even if it was necessary that he establish a foundation that calls to the Tawhid of Allah Almighty. And if he had no Shari'ah and no summons, then there was no statute drawn for those belonging to him in his cycle — so the successors would merely evaluate their drawings upon the drawing of the rest of the Pronouncers. This is a sick belief. It is not permissible to say that there was no revelation in that cycle nor any Shari'ah, because command and prohibition come by the inspiration of Allah, and the descent of Allah's command is revelation. And if command, prohibition, and revelation are established, then the Shari'ah is established as the manifestations of the statutes — which indicates that the first Speaker had a Shari'ah, in addition to what is indicated by
(1) In Version (B): "their differences" is given as "in adwarihim."
The Book of Riyadh [12]
- 177

<!-- page 180 -->
the necessary proof from what the wise have said. Allah said:
"And recite to them the news of the two sons of Adam in truth, when they offered a sacrifice — and it was accepted from one of them and not accepted from the other" (the verse).

The offering is one of the laws, and it is the most established of the reasons of the Shari'ah. Allah has commanded it in every Shari'ah, and He has made it the root of asceticism and purity. This is why the sacrifice is called a rite (mansak), as Allah says: "And for every nation We have appointed a rite" — and He said: "and to every nation We have appointed an act of devotion, that they may pronounce the name of Allah over what He has provided them of cattle, so let them not dispute with you" (the verse).

The place where the sacrifice is brought near, and in the hadith, the lame woman dragged her leg to the rite — the rite itself is the offering. A man is called a mansik (rite-keeper) when he is known by religion, piety, and purity. The offering is called nusuk (devotion) because it is the purpose of the duties of religion. The purpose of nearness to Allah Almighty is in every law and in all nations — or in the reasons of the Shari'ah — and it is called qurban (offering) because by it they draw near to Allah. Being near to Allah Almighty is the first cause of obedience, disobedience, disbelief, faith, command, and prohibition — and it is the first of the laws of the Shari'ah.

The author of al-Nusrah said:
The author of al-Islah has argued for proving the Shari'ah for Adam (peace be upon him) by Allah's saying: "And recite to them the news of the two sons of Adam in truth, when they offered a sacrifice." But the offering is only one of the statutes of the laws after the distinction between determination and Shari'ah has been made, and the strongest evidence of this is drawn from the poetry of the Arabs without an underlying interest. There is no argument here to establish what he wanted to prove, and the interpretation of this verse is not as he thought, because if the offering in this place referred only to something belonging to the apparent laws — whoever slaughtered sheep and camels — it would have been as he mentioned. But the command of the offering in this subject is something other than what is in the laws: namely, the establishment of the proofs from beneath their hands, and the establishment of those who will take their place when they leave this world. This story is apparent so that it may be interpreted by the wise, even if he had read this story to the end —
- 178

<!-- page 181 -->
because Adam (peace be upon him) had no Shari'ah, because none of his sons did well until Allah sent a raven to scratch in the earth to show him how to bury his brother's evil — that is, to hide the dead and bury him. If burial were among the laws, and Adam had a Shari'ah, he would not have had to be shown how. He would have had to place the body in its proper place or carry it according to the rite. That is what he said.

We say:
The Shari'ah of Adam (peace be upon him) has been proven by what the author of al-Islah argued in support of it, and what the author of al-Nusrah has mentioned does not invalidate it, because the author of al-Islah argued for proving the Shari'ah — which is one of the duties of speaking on the worship of Allah Almighty — by the way of knowing the reasons from the apparent meaning of the Book in the verse mentioning the sacrifice, and by the universally affirmative verse in which the Almighty says: "And for every nation We have appointed a rite, that they may pronounce the name of Allah" — and the other verse: "And to every nation We have appointed an act of devotion." Thus it is established that this is not as the author of al-Nusrah supposed, and that the matter in the interpretation of this verse is not as he thought; rather it contradicts (1) the statement of the reformer. The reformer did not argue for proving the Shari'ah by the interpretation of this verse, but by its outward sense. So the statement of the author of al-Islah is confirmed by the law of Adam (peace be upon him), and the response of the author of al-Nusrah does not contradict it; the Shari'ah remains fixed as it has been proven.

Chapter Two of Title IX

The author of al-Islah said:
If the offering is not among the laws that appear from
1 — Location per version (b) is special.
2 — It came in the (B) version of al-Nusrah.
- 179


<!-- page 182 -->
The slaughter of sheep and camels would have been as he mentioned. However, the command regarding offerings in this context is not part of the laws according to his interpretation, and it does not contradict the statement of the author of the Reform. Rather, it remains binding in the manner he has obligated, since he said nothing beyond what is established in the laws.

What appears, then, is the affirmation of the offering, for it is among the manifest duties of religion and Shari'ah. He had pushed the claim that what is meant must be the apparent sense, and this is a difficult position. What he said — that the offering in this place is not according to the apparent meaning of the Shari'ah — invalidates the statement of the author of the Reform. For what the author of Al-Nusra has said follows the course of an appeal that can only be proven by evidence, and it is permissible for its apparent meaning to exist just as its inner meaning exists. This is especially so since the verse does not follow the course of a parable whose interpretation must be sought while abandoning its apparent meaning. If that is the case, then all of the apparent senses in the verse remain operative, and the obligations of the Shari'ah of Adam (peace be upon him) are established.

Chapter Three of Title IX

Then the author of the Reform said:

The establishment of arguments from those under their hands and from those who take their place requires that Adam must have something to which he calls them, if proofs are to be established and arbiters to be appointed. Boundaries are established to summon to what the Speaker proclaims, and to set forth what serves the interest of those invited to God in this world, in religion, in the Hereafter, and in the beginning. Adam is not without it. Peace be upon him: he must be a father, since he prescribed the Shari'ah and enacted the obligations that serve as arbiter. He prescribed nothing, and showed none of the laws of worship, whether small or great. He would need to establish arguments and send forth preachers from among those who take his place if he did not maintain something requiring preservation, by which the nation is supported. With the affirmation of the author of Al-Nusra by interpretation, he has established arguments, and the Shari'ah and the obligations are binding, for the Shari'ah belongs to Adam upon him. Peace be upon you.

- 180

<!-- page 183 -->
Chapter Four of Title IX

Then we say:

When the need for the prophets (peace be upon them) was for the education of the nation — so that it might be happy with him in the Hereafter and in this world, and be guided to its interests in this world and in religion — then Adam (peace be upon him), being a prophet, must have been a teacher and a guide. If he must be a teacher and guide, then there must be that by which he teaches his nation what brings it happiness and guides it to its interests. If this must exist, then it can be nothing other than the laws of worship, which is the Shari'ah. For the Shari'ah of Adam upon him be peace is immutable. The truth of this is confirmed by Allah's saying (interpretation of the meaning): "The people were one nation" — in ignorance — "so Allah sent the Prophets as bearers of good tidings and warners, and He sent down the Book with them in truth, to judge between people in matters wherein they differed." So He confirmed the prophets, and if he was a prophet, God did not send him except to bear good news, to warn, and to judge by the Book. Good news, warning, judgment, and arbitration occur only by means of the obligations and prohibitions which constitute the Shari'ah, so it is established.

Chapter Five of Title IX

Sahib al-Nusrah said:

If he had read this verse to the end, he would have said that Adam had nothing belonging to him. One of his sons did not know what to do until the moment came when Allah sent a raven scratching the earth to show him how to bury his brother. If the burial of the dead in any manner were among the laws — and if Adam (peace be upon him) had a Shari'ah — he would not have concealed it from his sons. So this is a statement issued by someone without inquiry or examination.

- 181

<!-- page 184 -->
We say:

If the author of the Reform adopted the fallacy — like the fallacy of the author of Al-Nusra — in the chapter on the verse he invoked concerning the meaning of the sacrifice, when he said that the interpretation of the verse is as he thought, then the author of Al-Nusra would not be without his support, or he would have to make the verse he invoked regarding the establishment of the Shari'ah of Adam (peace be upon him) into a unique interpretation. In that, he invokes it, and his argument is invalidated in paying what he intends to pay from the law of Adam (peace be upon him). For on the face of the verse, his protest first turns it into an interpretation in the first place, and he conducts it according to what its apparent meaning conveys, so that it does not indicate anything of what he intended. The verse contains no indication that the son of Adam did not carve open the carcass of a crow — when in the earth he saw him, and he saw his brother and buried him, and the argument was established for him. The verse says: "So Allah sent a raven to scratch the ground, to show him how to hide his brother's corpse. He said: 'Woe to me! Am I unable to be like this crow and hide my brother's corpse?' And he became one of the regretful." It is mentioned that he saw him, but there is no evidence that he buried him.

Chapter Six of Title IX

The interpretation of the verse and its content also does not indicate everything of that. And that is because both the opponent and the guardian believe that in the worship of Allah Almighty there is something which is His sacrifice, by which one draws closer to Allah Almighty. For the opponent thinks that (1) worship is nothing but the apparent, namely from works, and that salvation is only in it, and this will be by belief and sincerity in him who takes the place of the prophet (peace). And the guardian believes that the worship of Allah Almighty is only in the outward — which is the work — and in the inward, which is knowledge, and that salvation is only in both of them together, and that the one who stands in the place of the prophet (peace) is from the feet of the Messenger (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) and his family. And they disputed in that

1 — It fell in copy (A).
- 182

<!-- page 185 -->
One day, they each argued before the Prophet, and each of them explained his belief concerning what he worships. This is what He said: "When they offered an offering, it was accepted from one of them" — meaning that each of them believes in what brings him closer to Allah Almighty, and that His Messenger has something to accept from one of them, which is the guardian, that is, he is pleased with him. The Speaker who stands in the place of God believes in God and in His worship, and does not accept from the other — who is the opponent — that is, the Speaker did not accept his belief, since he was on a different face. The Speaker was satisfied with what he accepted from the guardian's belief concerning himself.

However, he had outwardly to declare regret regarding the opponent, attributing the inclination to the guardian. Concerning this he said: "If I had honored you with Allah, I would have feared you," and the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) said: "Abu Bakr feared you," and he was able to hear it from him. The Prophet recited the verse that he read only to please his belief and his way, and that he was the one who stood up after him. He stood up, and in the heart of the opponent there was the conviction that he had overcome the guardian, and he said to him: "I will kill you, to push you away from this belief, since he did not accept it from you." And the matter — the guardian said to him: "Allah accepts only from the pious," meaning that the Guardian of God, who is the Messenger, takes no one's place, and is not satisfied with anyone, and no one believes — except among the pious who combine knowledge and action, and draw nearer to Allah Almighty by establishing all of its features. So the opponent deliberately challenged and stabbed the guardian, while not knowing anything. So they plead with the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding their belief, and he was satisfied with his belief. And the guardian said: "If you stretch out your hand to me to kill me, I shall not stretch out my hand to you to kill you. I fear Allah, the Lord of the worlds." You helped me, and let loose your tongue against me, and laid from my destiny, and said concerning another obligation: do not be satisfied with what I believe in the worship of Allah (1), the Lord of the Worlds, for I do not do as you do, nor do I challenge you, for I am under the command of the Spokesperson who is in the place of God — who is the master of the role, the Lord of the Imams — and under His obedience. I fear Him, and I do not give

1 – It fell in copy (a).
- 183

<!-- page 186 -->
He paid no heed to this saying from the guardian against him. So he abandoned what was [right] and obeyed him, and he killed his brother. His soul rose against the other, and he ran against him — the opponent, who would not be resolved, held back, or consulted except with him. That is, when he returned to the first opponent with what had happened to the second opponent, he told him: "Do not believe in God and in His worship except as I have said." What he said meant that the guardian is sharp, and that good for him is in the situation of the guardian — and that he is prevented from his rank, attributing to him that he does not improve anything. So he pushed him out of his rank, overcame him, and said: Worship is nothing except by this apparent meaning, nor by what he says to him. So he became one of the losers when he worshipped Allah by obeying the Speaker without obeying the Foundation, and the outward without the inward.

So Allah sent a raven to scratch the earth — that is, when the time was prolonged and it was time to act, the guardian wanted to establish the argument against the opponent, so that he would be separated from the world after a reminder. So He sent to him — which is His saying (1), "And Allah sent" — that is, the one in charge of the Speaker, who is the one who takes the place of Allah, sent a man from among his companions to explain to him his matter and his status, and what Allah Almighty has of a secret in His silence regarding the seeking of his right, and that He provides a way out for him from what he did. He longed to return the truth to its people. This is the meaning of the raven's search in the earth, to show him how to rid himself of what he had acquired against himself, and to guide him to duty. He is the man who was sent by the guardian of God for that purpose — Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr — for he is among those who are specially related to the guardianship from the side of religion, and to the opponent from the side of lineage. So Muhammad did what he was sent for, so that the opponent might be alerted to his crime, and led to abide by his mandate. So the second opponent prevailed over his opinion and prevented him from what he wanted to do. And he was sorry for the guardian, and said to himself: "O woe to me! Am I unable to be like this crow?" — that is, "I wish I were like this man," meaning Muhammad his son, who is a stranger to the guardian, and his example in keeping God's covenant, religion, and concealment of

1 — It fell into the shackles (A).
- 184

<!-- page 187 -->
the secrets of the guardian of God. So he became one of those who regret what he missed in following the guardian first, and in his deed, which will take him in the end to the abode of the Hereafter. We seek refuge in Allah from the annulment of the covenant. By way of protest against it, if this is so, then the author of Al-Nusra has nothing in his protest by means of this verse, except the saying of the author of the Reform, in which his duty is the Shari'ah obligations of Adam (peace be upon him).

Chapter Seven of Title IX

It has been mentioned that laws, dispensations, obligations, and customary practices may increase and decrease according to the time in which the Speaker arises, and according to what he needs for the reformation of the Ummah. Narrations have come down that washing the dead, embalming, shrouding, and burying them are from what Adam (peace be upon him) prescribed. If the reports concerning that have been repeated as mentioned, this verse — what was said about the mention of the raven and searching the ground when the son of Adam was killed — does not follow the course of parables whose interpretation must be sought, and its apparent meaning is not set aside. According to what we have done and put forth, the Shari'ah of Adam (peace be upon him) is established beyond dispute.

Chapter Eight of Title IX

Then we say:

Invoking this verse for the rejection of the obligations of Adam's law (peace be upon him) is invalidated. Burying the dead is not among the things whose obligations have increased — which are purity, prayer, zakat, and the other actions. With the loftiness of its standing comes the loftiness of all the other laws which are the foundations of worship. Rather, it is a kind of thing done with the dead: by burning with fire, or throwing into water,

- 185

<!-- page 188 -->
or carrying to a cave or desert, or burying in the ground, or feeding to the wild beasts. If it is a kind of practice of the Shari'ah, then it should not be the case that, with the loftiness of its rank, burial may be replaced by other things — which would invalidate the obligations of the Shari'ah altogether. But if he refrains from doing so, then the Shari'ah is proven for Adam (peace be upon him).

Chapter Nine of Title IX

The author of al-Nusrah said:

Adam (peace be upon him) was not the owner of a law, because if he had been the owner of a law, Allah would have commanded the angels to prostrate themselves through him.

We say:

The author of Al-Nusra has bound himself by saying that what would establish Adam (peace be upon him) as the owner of a Shari'ah is that Allah commanded the angels to prostrate — even if this is apparently not from the side of Adam (peace be upon him). It was only through him, as evidenced by the fact that the command — it is impossible for him [Adam] that they prostrate to him unless he is a Mustafa; and the command to prostrate to him is impossible unless he is a Mustafa. And it has been proven that he is a Mustafa, as Allah says (interpretation of the meaning): "Allah has chosen Adam and Noah" — the verse. If he is Mustafa, then it is impossible for Allah to command those who are without the Mustafa except through the Mustafa. So Allah commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam — it was only through him. And if it was through him, then the law is proven for him. That he said.

Chapter Ten of Chapter Nine

Then Allah commanded us to prostrate to Adam (peace be upon him) by saying, "Prostrate to Adam," as He commanded the Children of Israel when He said, "O Children of Israel, remember My grace which I have bestowed upon you."

- 186


<!-- page 189 -->
(1) "And fulfill My covenant, and I shall fulfill your covenant, and have awe of Me alone. And believe in what I have sent down, confirming what is with you, and be not the first to disbelieve in it, and do not sell My signs for a small price, and be mindful of Me. And do not confound the truth with falsehood, nor conceal the truth knowingly. Establish the prayer, give the zakat, and bow with those who bow."

If the verse appears in a form that does not indicate the presence of an intermediary, then by means of Muhammad it was nevertheless conveyed to them; and if it is possible to say that Muhammad is not the bearer of a law on this account, then (2) the verse — which mentions Allah's command to the Children of Israel — likewise indicates that the command came by means of him. For if the two verses were placed in the chapter of being non-indicative of a single authentic intermediary, this would be impossible; for the command of Allah Almighty to the Children of Israel, although outwardly devoid of any mention of (3) an intermediary, was only by means of Muhammad. And if that is impossible, then Adam too is the author of a sharee'ah, and the sharee'ah is established for him.

**Chapter Eleven of Title IX**

The author of al-Nusrah said:

The angels are not assigned and are not obligated by the Sharia, because they do not disobey Allah in the twinkling of an eye; rather, they glorify the praise of their Lord and do what they are commanded.

We say:

The angels who were charged with prostration — if they were not among those who bear assignment, they would not have been commanded to prostrate to Adam, nor would He have said to them, "Bow down to him." And the angels who bear no assignment are those who have never been in the abode of the body, nor have they stood (1) In copy (A) it was answered to me. (2) It fell in copy (A). (3) It fell in copy (A). - 187

<!-- page 190 -->
forth into the realm of deed. They were the foremost in the abode of eternity. What is meant here, however, are the angels who were appointed over the heavens, who dwelt in the house of nature and exercised dominion through the virtues that bear resemblance to those in the abode of eternity — the creative and prophetic angels — as we have shown previously, since only those in the house of creativity and rebirth advance in this way. As for prostration and bowing, these belong to the duties of worship and deeds, which exist only in the natural world. Those who are charged with establishing the two acts of worship are assigned to it so that, by means of them, they may receive the increase and the blessings of happiness with which Allah exalts their station, and they thereby attain the perfection that earns them eternity and survival. For this reason there was the commissioning of the angels and the call upon them to act.

**Chapter Twelve of Title IX**

The author of al-Nusrah said:

He said: If the prostration of the angels to Adam had been their law, Adam would have said: "God commands you to prostrate and to obey me," and he would have striven against those who disobeyed him in the command of God. This too applies to all pronouncements.

We say:

The author of al-Islah may reply: It is not the case that, because Adam did not say "God commands you to prostrate to me and to obey me," prostration must therefore not be an obligatory ordinance. For the Prophet did not say to the Children of Israel "God commands you to establish prayer and give me zakat," and yet there is no evidence that prayer, zakat, and all that he commanded them are not among the duties of sharee'ah. The laws are established by the fact that their bringer was a strivers; otherwise, Jesus (peace be upon him) would not have had a law sanctioned for him, since he did not strive — and this is not valid.

**Chapter Thirteen of Title IX**

The author of al-Nusrah said:

- 188

<!-- page 191 -->
Also, Allah Almighty did not mention in the Qur'an that Adam (peace be upon him) had a sending, nor did He mention his being sent as He did with others, when He said: "We sent Noah." Nor did He mention him in the verse of the Shari'ah, when He said: "He has prescribed for you of the religion that which He enjoined upon Noah, and that which We have revealed to you, and that which We enjoined upon Abraham, Moses, and Jesus — to establish the religion and not be divided therein." (1) The verse.

The author of al-Nusrah is not fair in his objection. Let it not be hoped that the author of al-Islah will say in his book: As for Adam, he is mentioned in the Qur'an, along with his followers and his people the angels — who were commanded to prostrate to him, and from whom they learned the names according to what Allah Almighty commanded, saying to him: "O Adam, inform them of their names." This act of informing is greater than mere sending, for the sending of messengers entails their being made the successors of Allah in His land, by which Allah refrains from realizing — and Allah Almighty wrote in His Book that He made him a Caliph on earth, to whom its people would return for what they need in the matter of their religions.

As for his not being mentioned in the verse that names the one who prescribed sharee'ah — as the author of al-Islah said, that he was not mentioned with them because he was not among the people of resolve and was not a man of determination — if it is permissible for Adam to be excluded from the group of the masters of (2) laws on the grounds that his name is not mentioned with the five (peace be upon them), then it is likewise permissible because he is not mentioned among those to whom revelation was sent, when the Almighty said: "We have revealed to you as We revealed to Noah and the prophets after him, and We revealed to Abraham, Ishmael, Isaac, Jacob, the tribes, Jesus, Job, Jonah, Aaron, and Solomon." The verse — would make him fall outside their sentence as well, and that is impossible. So the saying is the saying of the author of al-Islah, taken from him.

<!-- page 192 -->
**Chapter XIV of Title IX**

The author of al-Nusrah said:

We must also know the reason for the existence of sharee'ah, so that it may be true. We can then say that Adam (peace be upon him) did not have a law.

We say:

The reason for the obligation of the Shari'ah is the neglect of the limits, their disruption, and the pursuit of their opposites by creation — but their claim to this is something Allah did not bring about in him. This meaning did not appear in Adam's time, for the world that was before him and his people were two neighbors on the boundary, and none of them violated a single limit, as they themselves declared when they said: "Will You place in it one who corrupts it and sheds blood, while we glorify You with praise and sanctify You?" (the verse). Why then should Adam have to establish the Shari'ah, given this?

We say:

The reason for the necessity of the existence of the Shari'ah is different from what the author of al-Nusrah said when he claimed that the limits are neglected, that they are disrupted, and that creation follows opposites. That is not the ground of obligation for a sharee'ah, nor does it establish it. Rather, we say on our own behalf: As for the reason for the necessity of the existence of sharee'ah — which is the ordinances of deeds — we have explained it in our book known as al-Masabih fi al-Imamah (Lamps in the Imamate). The closest thing to the need of the people is first their reliance, in their survival, on what guards them against destruction — the ordinances by which blood is preserved, and (1) by which their hearths and wealth are fortified. By them they are saved in matters of necessity that arise among them. If these ordinances did not exist, their affairs would come to a halt and they would destroy one another: the strong, in the absence of restraint, would tyrannize through his rage and through what he holds of money and other goods, and the fires of strife would be kindled among them. To refrain from this matter in wisdom, the Almighty Maker must enact what guards them from destruction constantly — which is the Sharia, if its existence is necessary.

1 - In copy (A) it is stated (and to be saved) - 190

<!-- page 193 -->
**Chapter XV of Title IX**

Then we say:

But its existence — that is, the drawing of the laws — has become a necessary existence, because the souls that belong to human beings each do not refrain from one another (which is what is specialized) and (1) from these acts that are indispensable to the ordinances which the community uses to silence the cessation of their dealings. By these ordinances they secure one another, since the ordinances are necessary.

We say:

Some of them are necessary at all times and seasons, and some of them are not. What is necessary may exist at one time and not at another (2), and increase or decrease. What is necessary is such matters as drawing near to Allah and drawing strength: retribution in the case of persons, the ordinance of marriage, the division of money such as inheritance and the like, the ordinance for the absent and the dead, and the ordinance for the extraction of rights and their return to their masters. For human beings have three souls: the rational soul, which has discrimination and thought — it knows that it has a Creator and naturally submits to Him, and from this draws near to Him. As it draws near, it is compelled to enact ordinances that demand most of these things, and these ordinances are many — or so it is said. Then there is the irascible soul that he possesses, by which he is angered when he is angered, and which loves to subdue, conquer, take revenge, oppress, kill, and deceive — so that he is compelled to enact an ordinance by which he is restrained with great force (3), so that they may be separated from one another, and the rights of the oppressed may be taken from the aggressor by force, whether in the body by retribution or by other means. And lust — from which he seeks refuge and seeks marriage as a necessity — so he is compelled to enact ordinances that remove the

1 - The sentence is completely omitted in copy (A). 2 - Fell in copy (A) (3) Fell in copy (a) - 191

<!-- page 194 -->
cessation arising from the jealousy among them that would lead them to death. This soul demands all wealth for itself in any way it can, so it must be restrained by ordinances by which they trust one another against cheating, cunning, and deceit, which would otherwise lead them to domination and fighting. These souls move with their eagerness to seek sustenance, and transactions become necessary, so they are compelled to work; for treachery and cunning are by nature, and ordinances are needed by which the plaintiff and the defendant run their course in extracting the truth for its owner. Death is necessary among them, and they cannot do without a means of dealing with the absence of the dead: either by burial, burning, or being cast away in a friendly manner — otherwise harm would come, and he is compelled to adopt one of these actions. These are six gates through which the categories of necessity run, beneath which lie the kinds whose existence is necessary among human beings without fail. As for what is not necessary, and is at one time more and at another less, these are the duties of worshipping Allah, may He be exalted, and drawing closer to Him through knowing His limits, by which perfection is attained. These fall under the category of drawing closer to Allah. All these ordinances belong to the Shari'ah, and it is necessary to enact them first and to inscribe them among human beings at the beginning of their existence. If these ordinances existed in the time of Adam (peace be upon him) — who was one of the human beings — and his angels were among them, then the laws of Islam are established for him.

**Chapter Sixteen of Title IX**

But whoever was before Adam, his ruling is the ruling of those who are at the end of the seventh cycle, for example, in a manner that is not free of the necessary ordinances we have mentioned. He was free, however, of the ordinances that fall under the genus of worship in drawing nearer to Allah Almighty — those which we have said may increase at one time and decrease at another, and by which the second perfection is attained. So Allah sent Adam (peace be upon him) to teach them and others — for unless they were taught, they would fall short, even though they are distinguished above others by virtue, and they would fall short of the degree of perfection by leaving off the work of worship. So he prescribed, believed, and called for the two acts of worship in knowledge and deed, and some of them followed and obeyed,

- 192

<!-- page 195 -->
while some of them abstained and turned back upon the previous six at the beginning of the cycles. This is the order of those people.

**Chapter Seventeen of Title IX**

The author of al-Nusrah said:

But Noah (peace be upon him) had to establish it — meaning the Shari'ah — because before his cycle they played at violating the limits and following opposites, such as al-Wadd, al-Suwa', al-Jawooth, and others. So it was obligatory for Noah (peace be upon him) to establish it, so that whoever perished would perish with knowledge, and whoever lived would live with knowledge.

We say:

This statement does not entail that Adam must have no law; rather, he too must have duties and a sharee'ah. For it has been established as obligatory that the role of violating the limits and following opposites — and violation only falls to one who follows another by abandoning his command and his ordinance — and the violation was proved by the saying that the ordinances became the Shari'ah, and by which the violation occurred to Adam (peace be upon him). So the Shari'ah

Nada Sur Azbakiya

is established for him.

**Chapter Eighteen of Title IX**

The author of al-Islah said:

It was narrated that Allah Almighty commanded Adam (peace be upon him) to set up a tent. He brought it down from Paradise and made it his qiblah and the qiblah of his son. Then Seth built a place after him — the Shari'ah, its wisdom, the collection of revelation and interpretation therein, the establishment of its branches and origins, and the arbitration of its obligations.

We say:

The Book of Riyadh [13]

The saying of the author of al-Islah is established — that Adam has a law and ordinances like the others among the pronouncements.

**Chapter Nineteen of Title IX**

The saying of the author of al-Nusrah:

In the structure and organization of the world, in the chapter of signifying monotheism, it is indispensable to have ordinances of conduct and station; and the modes of conduct and signs have removed many of the moralists from monotheism and cast them into anthropomorphism — and this is exceedingly impossible. The structure of the world, the systems and wonders of His wisdom, what lies in the composition of the world of bodies, the composition of bodies, and the pairing of opposite natures in the different bodies — and the persons destined to signify monotheism — make it indispensable to enact verbs, similar actions, and different situations that signify agreed-upon meanings; and proverbs represented by an existing parable, and proofs based on a clear connotation. What lies in these evidences and in the contradictory deeds along the apparent way, and what lies in these proverbs that are multiplied to establish known boundaries, is evidence of monotheism itself — because the elaborate and intricate actions of the world are wondrous, and souls sing of deeds and signs. And indeed, many of these signs, deeds, and outward words have removed most of the people from monotheism, and cast them into anthropomorphism that is not fitting for the least of His creatures. The conclusion is that there is a composition of the world and its systems in the chapter of signifying monotheism, which is indispensable to the station of works; and the situation of deeds and signs has removed many of creation from monotheism and cast them into anthropomorphism.

We say:

If he says this, then it is obligatory to send the messengers — and this is a virtue for which he has no need of them.

- 194


<!-- page 197 -->
If the world is itself an elaborate proof, it serves as an indication of monotheism, and the sending of the messengers (1) to call to and signify monotheism — sending them with such evidence — would mean that they are doing what others already accomplish, which is a virtue God has no need of. I do not know how this could be claimed for Him, when the apparent order of the world is already an arbiter. Is that not sufficient to indicate tawhid? If it is not sufficient on its own, then He teaches and demonstrates it; and one benefits from knowing the structure of the world, its systems, and its arrangement. There exist those whose station has risen in knowledge through being taught the limits — how to perform the works, the signs the revelation gathers, and the law — so they reflect, deduce, and infer from him what one ought to know of the limits of Allah and His presumed verses. Humans must know this, as Allah says: "Even if they came, he says, you have denied My signs and did not take note of them" — though if you knew, the foremost in existence are the honorable jewels who are the angels nearest to Him. So too is the matter when there is need of works, signs, alerting, and education, since not all attain to the knowledge, action, and alertness from which one can deduce the truth of inference. How much less if one does not know at all? In sum, the claim that leads to the disruption of the degrees of the limits is a statement neither from our belief nor from the doctrine of our loyalists, may Allah's peace and blessings be upon them. Perhaps this statement has been planted by adversaries in the book so it might be attributed to the author of the book — and Allah knows best.

Chapter Twenty of Title IX

Furthermore, the work is not only for monotheism, but also for the correction of the soul in worship, for emulating the highest assembly, and for acquiring through discipline the honorable morals and noble habits by which they prepare for union with what is above them — not to be diverted from the way.

(1) Dropped in copy (A).
— 195

<!-- page 198 -->
The power that preserves the honor of the intellect by fulfilling its duties and that is preoccupied with its features — if it were not for the deeds and rituals of the Ummah, and the wholeness of souls within it through perseverance, souls would perish. Therefore Allah did not respond to the angels when they imagined that what they were doing of worship was sufficient at the door of closeness to God Almighty and to their perfection, and that they had no need of a caliph who would teach them or command them to do anything; for He said: "I know what you do not know." The Almighty spoke thus because the universes, by His decree and His wisdom, are between force and act — hesitating: sometimes standing in potentiality, and sometimes already existing in actuality. The thing, when it reaches its end in one state, must necessarily return to Him from force and act in retrograde — if from force to act, and if already in act, then back to force. It is like heat: when heat reaches its end in the body, cold appears, as in the melting of bodies and the like; and when cold reaches its end, cold ceases and heat appears, as with snow; and likewise the gathering of its parts from the mountains, which, when its gathering reaches its end, is the nightingale's season, and dissolution appears in its parts, so they disperse and return to sand, and that changes. This is among the beings in the abode of nature, and so too were knowledge and ignorance in the world of the universe. Corruption is sometimes ignorance, and knowledge is powerful, in the sense that ignorance is general in the presence of its people, and ignorance (3) is lost through the lack of its people. The time was the time in which ignorance had taken hold and already reached its end, and knowledge had been introduced, and reached its end in potentiality. The teachers were disturbed, the ceremonies of the laws were disrupted, the deeds were prolonged in duration, and the times were shortened. By "the laws" I mean what cannot be without its presence among the rituals and rites; and by "the angels" I mean those in themselves the best of them, whose virtues are the bearers of knowledge in that age, and those who worship Allah. They narrated that this was sufficient for him in the chapter of worship and perfection — and it was

— 196

<!-- page 199 -->
that the matter was different from what they estimated, since they needed knowledge of the limits in totality. Those in the house of creativity and the first rebirth, and the knowledge of those who come late in existence, are like the second revival, and they must act by what earns them. When they knew that their time was the time of the complete role of ignorance, that they were not in the role of knowledge nor in the role of works, the Almighty taught them to leave them as they were — when ignorance reaches its end as the purpose of the time, since time is the time of the beginning of knowledge by its appearance, which is what wisdom requires. The Almighty said: "I know" the end (1) of ignorance in the world up to its end, the act, the completion of its role, and its appearance; and the attainment of knowledge in the world up to its goal in strength; and the return of repentance to Him in the reappearance; and the resurrection of the need in His appearance for the establishment of teachers and guides — "what you do not know." So Allah sent Adam, peace be upon him, making him His successor to show forth knowledge, to bring them integrity in actuality, to show them how to know the boundaries, and to teach them what they did not know. This was the beginning of the matter — the emergence of knowledge from power into act in the presence of its people from his days, peace be upon him. Its end extends to the one who arises, peace be upon him; and it is also said that when the one who arises, peace be upon him, appears, knowledge has already become — meaning that it is widespread, and its people will multiply, while ignorance is internalized, meaning that its people are reduced and its root is cut off. The treasures of the earth appear in his days, and he casts them to their appearance, which is a sign of the one who arises — until knowledge is already established, and he discloses all that has been deposited in the bellies of the revealed books and complex symbols. And if the angels, with the presence of the heavens and the good ordering of them, had mastered the structure of the world's assets, they would still not have known, nor would they have attained perfection, and there would be no inference from it — except for what Adam, peace be upon him, uncovered and called them to. What the author of Al-Nusra mentioned was uninvestigated. It was

deeds, signs, and proverbs that are indispensable in the chapter of inference

of some of them concerning monotheism, politics, self-correction, and their discipline in knowing and bringing them out into action (1). If that is so, then Adam is the author of a Shari'ah and customs to which he called, and which indicated the limits of Allah and His unity.

Chapter Twenty-One of Title IX

The author of al-Nusrah said:

The author of this article says that the creation in the great role did not know — for was there not a similar apparent law among them? Or would one say that the one responsible for it, peace be upon him, in the raising of the laws represented a nullification of the knowledge of monotheism, and the people went out to a saying that it is obstructed? If the creation is not ignorant of monotheism, and not ignorant of the role of the Qa'im, and they likewise do not know him because the laws have been raised, then it would have been permissible for Adam, peace be upon him, to have called people to monotheism (2) without any references — and the like of this in saying.

And we say:

It may precede our discussion of knowledge and ignorance, and the fact that each of them is sometimes by force and sometimes by act — indeed, this involves explaining the situation in which the creation found itself during the great role, being at the end of ignorance, according to the saying of the author of Al-Nasra. Adam's call (peace be upon him) and his being a teacher to his followers in the landmarks of monotheism would not have been needed, because the people must already have known monotheism. And if they knew (3) the monotheism, then Adam's invitation to them would not have been to do anything they already knew — which would be nothing but a virtue God did not need, and that is impossible.
