— 198

<!-- page 201 -->
The people did not need what they already had for themselves. When Allah sent Adam, He made him His successor among them — chose him from among them, appointed him as His caliph — and made it obligatory for them to obey him and to return to him in what they did not know. Rather, it was the saying of the angels, "We praise You and sanctify You," in their estimation that they were adequate in praise, sanctification, and monotheism, and that what they were in was sufficient in the matter of worship and knowledge of the limits. But Allah knew what He commanded — what His mercy obliged — to choose Adam from among them, and sent him to them so as to make him a caliph in their education, calling them to their perfection of work and knowledge, all of which leads to knowing the limits in which tawhid is valid. Therefore He said: "I know what you do not know," because the Almighty knew that they were imperfect, that ignorance had ended in the deed, that the work had come to manifest, and that they did not know. This is why it is obligatory in wisdom to establish the office of education, which is the cause of the expansion of knowledge and the multitude of its people. So Allah selected Adam, gave him a law, and taught him, as Allah said: "And Adam knew all the names, then He showed them to the angels and said: Inform Me of the names of these, if you are truthful. They said: Glory be to You — we have no knowledge except what You have taught us; You are the Knower, the Wise. He said: O Adam, tell them their names. … I know the unseen of the heavens and the earth" — the verse. The people were of two worlds, and because they were so, Adam came to them as their teacher.

Chapter Twenty-Two of Title IX

We say:

As for his saying and his affirmation that the creation was not, at first, in the role of the Qa'im (Sal'am) ignorant of monotheism — that if they were not ignorant, they could only deduce it from the side of the supporters, which includes the integrity of themselves and their images — when they were selected from

— 199

<!-- page 202 -->
among them, Adam, so that he would be the caliph of God Almighty in teaching them what is in their interests sooner and later — it is impossible to conceive this perception in them and yet give them a status that would be theirs. And his saying, "and not in the role of the one who arises are they ignorant" — if what he means is the image of the da'wah from the role of the Qa'im before it appears and before it exists from the natural world, when it is preserved by his successors and preachers after the completion of the role of Muhammad al-Mustafa (Salam) and until his time, and the appearance of His signs in the world — then it is true, for then knowledge has raised the beacon of his appearance with the many scholars. This is the time in which Allah said: "On the day when the children will grow old." But if what he meant by his saying was that they are not ignorant in the role of the guardian after the Qa'im (Salam), who is the owner of the seventh floor, when he dismissed speech, distinguished the people of Paradise from the people of Hell, closed the door of education, and when repentance is no longer valid — because they do not remain knowledgeable, and they are not of the people of knowledge, for that time is the time of the waters to overflow and cover, and the time of misery and austerity to be seized and to appear — then the words of the author of Al-Nusra in that regard are not of an investigator.

Chapter Twenty-Three of Title IX

In summary, the author of Al-Nusra only mentioned these sayings and quotes in support of the owner of the crop in his payment of the law of Adam. Adam is not devoid of his supplication to them, and being a calm prophet — he must either have called them to encourage them toward Paradise and the neighbor of the Lord of the Worlds, or invited them to intimidate them toward Hell and being kept away from the mercy of the best of creators, or all of these. If He calls them to encouragement, encouragement is not perceptible except by striking

(1) The sentence is omitted in its entirety in copy (A).
— 200

<!-- page 203 -->
proverbs and reports about Him with what is known to the senses of the kinds of pleasures, blessings (1), and good places — such as dwellings, orchards, rivers, and trees — so they may conceive of it. That is the form of speech that requires interpretation. And if He called them to intimidation, then his saying is likewise only by giving them proverbs that frighten them, from it to the world of the senses, to visualize it; and in its interpretation there is a current other than the above. If He calls them to all of these, then his words are not without a valid apparent meaning, so interpretation is necessary. If that is the case, then the three sections affirm an apparent meaning that is fixed for Adam, followed by an interpretation — so Adam is the owner of a law and a clear custom.

Chapter Twenty-Four of Title IX

Then we say:

Adam, peace be upon him, is not without either calling the people of his time to obey God — obeying Him with wisdom — or without wisdom; and he does not disobey, for that is impossible. The belief that he is outside religion is impossible; rather he calls them to wisdom, and wisdom requires knowledge as well as work. So Adam is the owner of a law that combines knowledge and action. They are the worship of Allah, and through them he attains perfection and ascent to the houses of dignity.

Chapter Twenty-Five of Title IX

Regarding the one who arises (peace be upon him) and the saying that he raises the laws:

We say:

To believe this is sick, for the estimation of its existence from the natural world does not arise from the second way of revival, because it does not invalidate anything related to the worship of Allah, the Almighty. Rather, it is the conclusion of the roles of the predecessors and the completion of something that has been done in its place; and it removes the boundaries about their ranks, by the fact that the referendum took place in teaching about them, and the matter was completed in

(1) Dropped in copy (A).
— 201


<!-- page 204 -->
the new creation, regarding which Allah Almighty said: "Are We then wearied with the first creation?" — after He has established a judgment concerning the souls of one from whom the course of the foundations is derived,
those whose roles are emptied. And Allah Almighty said, describing the Master of the Day of Resurrection:
[When the heaven is cleft asunder (1) and when the planets are scattered (2)]. He said: "When the heaven is cleft asunder (1),
when the sun is darkened, when the stars fall, when the mountains are removed, and when the public…"
All these parables are multiplied upon the limits, and the references concern their passing away,
their ranks, not the laws and ordinances of the works that have passed in their time.
It studies its features without teachers, except what was necessary for its existence, as we have mentioned.
So proceed, for that is the time when this act appears with the closing of the door of
teaching, and the cessation of the calls on the part of the Master of the Great Resurrection. It is the beginning when
knowledge returns to potentiality and is concealed, and ignorance begins to increase. This has already been treated.
The appearance of the signs in this manner is sufficient for us, and Allah and the community of believers,
those of the people of divine goodness, by following his guardians. And we were gathered together with Muhammad and Ali
and the pure Imams (peace and blessings of Allah be upon them), the lights of His purity, His mercy upon His mercy.

Chapter Twenty-Six of Title IX

The author of al-Nusrah said:
Whoever says that monotheism (3) can be realized only through signs and works has refuted himself by
ruling that the First Intellect, the Soul, the angels, the Jadd, the Fath, and the Khayal
did not know Tawhid, since they have no signs or works between them or among them.

We say:
Whoever says this does not mean the First Intellect, nor the high limits.
(1) In copy (b) it is mentioned as (al-Shaqt).
(2) In copy (b) it appeared as (al-Taturt).
(3) The sentence is omitted in copy (a).
— 202

<!-- page 205 -->
Rather, he means the intellects in the world of the body, which is the second emanation, as it was its means.
Wholeness is attained by the teaching (1) of obligation, knowledge, signs, and works, and by
acquisition. The First Intellect and the paradoxical transcendent limits of bodies have not attained
their perfection through any of that; rather, they have gained their perfections from the beginning of their existence in innovation
and emanation. It is not permissible to apply this statement (2) to that. And what
the author of al-Nusrah mentioned regarding the meaning of the seven stars, their confirmation, their return, and their rectitude,
and the six days in which Allah created the heavens and the earth and all that is between them, and what is mentioned
of determination — the author of al-Islah did not leave anything that he did not bring from the interpretation of that
and its meanings. It has enough Arabization in the interpretation that it is hardly balanced (3),
it does not match.

Chapter Twenty-Seven of Title IX

The author of al-Islah said:
The first line is not obligatory until the second line appears, because the line
indicates the Speaker (nāṭiq), and the ʿarḍa indicates the Sharī'a, and a form should not appear
of a thing except after it has been completed. So, just as the ʿarḍa appeared after the second line, likewise
the law of the first was not fulfilled until the appearance of the second Speaker; and when the second Speaker appeared,
the law of the first is fulfilled, and its form appears in perfection. The same applies to the six ʿarḍas
in the seven lines, because there is no law before the first pronunciation, and no law upon the appearance of the
seventh — but the six laws belong to the pronouncers, the seventh of whom is the Qā'im. If you
draw seven lines, six of which appear in these parables,
one, two, three, four, five, six — even if the measurement is upon that,
(1) It fell in copy (A).
(2) In copy (B) "the intellects" appeared.
(3) In copy (B) it appeared as (balanced).
— 203

<!-- page 206 -->
to say that the first pronouncement has no law, then five ʿarḍas must appear
between seven lines. When six ʿarḍas appeared from among seven lines,
the seven lines became the masters of the seven cycles, and the six ʿarḍas
the six laws, and the law was made obligatory upon Adam.

The author of al-Nusrah said:
Concerning the chapter on the six ʿarḍas between the seven lines, and his inference from the lines
upon the Prophets, and from the ʿarḍas upon the six laws — it is not as he said.
Rather, the seven lines stand for the higher letters, since every Prophet wrote a letter
of them; and the six ʿarḍas stand for the cycles of the Imams between Adam and Noah,
who are the seven Imams; and between Noah and Abraham in the second cycle; and between Abraham and Moses
in the third cycle; and so on up to Muhammad (M). No other cycle remains for the two
Qā'ims save the cycle of their successors and their substitutes in the world. So six
ʿarḍas of five lines fell, as though there occurred between the cycles of the Imams five pronouncements of
the masters of the laws, in this likeness:
Adam — Noah — Abraham — Moses — Jesus — Muhammad — al-Qā'im.
the asās, the asās, the asās, the asās, the imams, the imams, the imams.
Just as the Qā'im (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) has no Imams after him, he is not charged with establishing
the Sharī'a; likewise, when there were no Imams before Adam (peace be upon him), he was not charged with
establishing the Sharī'a. For if the Sharī'a, in its establishment, must be preceded by Imams,
it is also delayed by them. And the asās of Noah (peace be upon him) preceded the cycle of Adam's asās (peace
be upon him), so he was followed by Imams, and thus he had to establish the Sharī'a.
Abraham, Moses, Jesus, Muhammad (peace be upon them) and al-Qā'im (may Allah be pleased with him) were preceded by
the cycle of Muhammad (peace be upon him), and he was not followed by Imams, so he did not have to establish the Sharī'a.
Likewise, Adam was followed by his asās, and no other Imams preceded him, so he was not required to
establish the Sharī'a. This is what they say.
— 204

<!-- page 207 -->
We say:
The statement of the author of al-Islah is identical to what he has indicated, but his saying that
"just as the ʿarḍa appeared after the second line, so the law of
the first was not fulfilled except with the appearance of the second Speaker" — this is a sick and incorrect statement.
The law of Adam is itself its foundation, and he has established its foundation for it. Even if it were permissible that the law of
Adam was fulfilled only with the coming of the Speaker of the second cycle, then it could be said that
the law of Muhammad is not perfected except with the coming of the Qā'im who holds the
seventh cycle (peace be upon him). This is among the impossibilities of statements, for the Sharī'a is a stature that does not
require any increase upon it nor any decrease from it. Even if the author of al-Islah said:
the first cycle, which belongs to Adam (peace be upon him), was not fulfilled except with the appearance of the Speaker of
the second cycle, which is Noah (peace be upon him) — and likewise the cycles are not a cycle
except with the appearance of what follows — then he made the location of his statement about the Sharī'a in the first cycle.
It would have been consistent. And Allah forgives us and him through His mercy.

Chapter Twenty-Eight of Title IX

As for the author of al-Nusrah's statement concerning the line (1) and the ʿarḍa, and his interpretation of the six ʿarḍas
upon the Imams — it is better that the formations be upon the pronouncers and not upon the higher
letters, and that the ʿarḍas be based upon the duration of their command in the cycle, not upon the asāses; otherwise it does not require
that Adam has no Sharī'a. Rather, the Sharī'a is made obligatory by the presence of the Imams after him.
The presence of the Imams entails the obligation to preserve the rank of the Speaker, his Sharī'a, and his designs in
his community; without that, there would be no obligation to obey the Imam of a Speaker-cycle. The five lines
and the six ʿarḍas — the author of al-Islah may take them and place the lines upon
the five Imams, and the ʿarḍas upon the cycles of the masters of the six laws, because
(1) Fell in copy (b).
— 205

<!-- page 208 -->
the first one in interpretation is that the thing must be identical and balanced if it is said and likewise replaced
in the souls — yes.

In the sentence we say:
The cycle is rotation: a major cycle and a minor cycle. The major cycle belongs to the Speakers,
those who preserve their place in their community after the Imams; and the minor cycle belongs to the faithful asāses,
those who seal the weeks. If the lines are given to the people of the cycles
who are the major ones — namely the Speakers — then the ʿarḍas would only be about the duration of the politics of their community.
On the other hand, the asās after them, in his cycle which seals it, awaits the coming of another like him, and known is
its amount. And if they are given to the seven minor ones, who are the Imams
in every cycle, then the ʿarḍas would only be for the duration of the order of the Imams in every
week and their complements who are rotated in the seventh; and known are their number and the number of Imams in
each cycle, and the number of suffixes according to the assets of the higher bodies described.
You will recall that in books other than this one, with the permission of Allah.

Chapter Twenty-Nine of Title IX

The author of al-Nusrah said:
For example, the words of Allah Almighty ("As We began the first creation, We shall repeat it") — it means as it was at the beginning of the matter,
which was not in terms of realities; so it is the final matter.

We say:
Even if this is an interpretation, the proper face is to say what corresponds to the saying
of Allah Almighty. This is a reference to the return of the Qā'im (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) after him.
Knowledge, after it has gone out into actuality, returns to potentiality; its abundance to scarcity; and the destinies of
all people after him become as they were in the time of Adam. And the return of ignorance after it had been in
— 206

<!-- page 209 -->
strength, and its reduction to actuality, and its abundance — because of its estimated wisdom. And blessed
be Allah, the best of creators.

Chapter Thirty of Title IX

The author of al-Nusrah said:
And also, if the author of al-Islah looked at what is in his name — I mean Adam — of the significance,
yet he had no law, because he had this: that his name is from three
letters, which are Alif, Dal, and Mim, which are not compounded or composed, but rather each
one of them is indicated by the other — a clear indication that he was not the master of
the authorship of the Sharī'a. And the five Prophets who were after him have names, each of which is the author of
a vehicle — such as Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad (peace be upon them) — which is evidence that
each of them had a Sharī'a. This is what he said.

We say:
If the separation of the letters of Adam's name entails that
Adam has no law, then the fact that these letters are not separate in themselves entails
that he has a law — because the Alif of the name is composed of alif, lām, and fā';
and the Mīm of it is composed of mīm, yā', and mīm; and likewise the Dāl. If separation is
not obligatory for him to have a law, then non-separation was obligatory for a law — provided that inference
in such a way is impossible; it is not true. For if it were true, it would be necessary that
the one who is responsible for the authorship of the Sharī'a is the author of the Qur'an, and his name, according to what is reported,
is — the Prophet (peace be upon him) is Muhammad — and Muhammad is composed of four letters.
It is impossible for him to be the master of a law, with his name being composite. Therefore, it is not possible that
the separation of the letters of Adam's name indicates that he is not the author of the law.
It is also invalidated that the joining of the letters of the name of the Qā'im (peace be upon him), who is Muhammad,
— 207

<!-- page 210 -->
by the fact that it is a compound, indicates that he is the author of the law. If that is invalidated, then it is not considered
by inference like this. The Sharī'a for Adam is fixed. And praise be to Allah, the Lord of the Worlds.

Chapter Thirty-One of Title IX

The author of al-Islah said:
As for the statement that Noah (peace be upon him) was the first to establish its foundation, and he was likened
to the ship — it has been said in the chapter on the foundations that there is sufficiency in it.

We say:
Rather, Noah was singled out by the ark because he was the first to have intentions, and the first
to abrogate the laws and compose a new law. His law was likened to
the ship, which he was copied with as the flood, because he destroyed the people of the earth with it
except those who responded to his law and boarded his ship — that is, established obedience to his foundation.
This means that his law lasted his lifetime; so when he completed it, he delegated the matter to its foundation
and commanded him to establish the call according to his law, and commanded the appendices to listen to him.
They did not receive the worship except through him. Whoever obeyed his foundation was in the ship,
and whoever disobeyed him and adhered to the first law — do you not see that he was described as
drowned by the flood — those who worshipped Wadd, Suwāʿ, Yaghūth, and Yaʿūq,
and Nasr? It is said: "They were drowned in their sins, so they were made to enter the Fire."

The author of al-Nusrah said:
If the status of the ship is the same as that of the apparent law, then he who adheres to it has survived,
being among the people of the apparent; and the true hidden call has been annulled — provided that
what appears from the Book of Allah Almighty is different from what the author of al-Islah went to.
Likewise, Allah Almighty described the beginning of the command of Noah (peace be upon him) and sent him to
his people, and he called them to his law, and then He ordered him to make the Ark. But these
— 208


<!-- page 211 -->
The proper account in Surat Hud confirms that, even if the ark stood for the apparent sharia, God would not have commanded Noah to build the ark first. Rather, the story shows that he first composed the apparent sharia, called creation to make use of it, and only then ordered him to build the ark — meaning that he was to establish his guardian (wali). The evidence is the saying of Allah, may He be exalted: "And he was making the ark," and likewise: "And whenever any of the chiefs of his people passed him, they ridiculed him," meaning that whenever Noah (peace be upon him) issued a command, the nobles of his people mocked him and marveled at him because he was the first to establish a guardian — and so they ridiculed him. This is what they said.

We say:

As for the statement of the author of al-Islah, with his interpretation of the ark as the face of the new sharia — because whoever entered under its rulings became like one inside a ship who is delivered from humiliation, abasement, and every kind of calamity, just as one who is inside a ship is delivered — this meaning is admissible. As for the author of al-Nusrah and his interpretation of the ark as the daʿwa and the guardian — because whoever enters the quiet daʿwa and adheres to obedience to its foundation has been kept safe from drowning in error, from the unity (tawhid) of Allah Almighty, and from knowledge of His limits, the guardian taking for him the rank of a guide — both interpretations are sound in that regard. One is the matter of this world and the other is the matter of religion (lit. brothers), and neither of them dispenses with the other, for each of them lifts up the head of the other.

Chapter Thirty-Two of Title Nine

As for the statement of the author of al-Nusrah, that Noah was the first to establish a guardian by interpretation in the new role, this is not correct, for the prophecy of Adam (peace be upon him) and his sharia are established. It is proven that Seth (peace be upon him) was his guardian, and the precedent is in the sharia, the guardianship, and its endurance is through him. It is from the dictates of reason that each
The Book of Riyadh [14]
— 209

<!-- page 212 -->
speaker (natiq) requires a guardian who derives benefit from him, particularly since every motor (muharrik) requires a necessary mover, the mover being one even if many things are moved by it. And since the speaker in his age is a source from which inspiration flows to all souls by his summons to seek persistence through the performance of the two acts of worship, it is necessary that there be a movable agent from whom the course of the learner runs, even if many learners learn from him — and the learner intended here is the one whom we call the guardian. Adam, when he was a speaker, was bound to have a guardian; and likewise every speaker. And if Adam has had a guardian appointed for him, it is not permissible to believe in anything contrary to that.

Chapter Thirty-Three of Title Nine

The author of al-Nusrah said:

After narrating what Allah Almighty said as a story concerning the son of Noah — "I will take refuge in a mountain that will protect me from the water," and Noah's reply, "There is no preserver today from the command of Allah" — he claimed that the matter was before Noah's time in successive stages, and the son did not know the rank of the guardian; and that if Adam had had a guardian, his son would have known about it. This is what he said.

We say:

This statement of his contradicts what he himself said in the chapter on cycles (al-adwar): that the imams took up the cycle of Adam (peace be upon him) after him. I do not know how this escaped him. I think that the copy of the book has been altered and added to, and that those who undertake the matter of religion are negligent in correcting what they write by listening and reading it back to the people of knowledge and religion — and Allah is the helper. The interpretation of "the son of Noah" is that the son attributed to
— 210

<!-- page 213 -->
Noah was not from his loins, but rather was a man of great worldly station whom he presented — like the opposite (al-mukhalif) in the cycle of Muhammad, our prophet. He benefited from Noah, learned what he had, and through his own influence became his "son." He took it upon himself, and people too imagined that he was his guardian.

Then the command of Allah Almighty came to make the ark — that is, the matter (amr) of Noah, for the guardianship was conferred upon another, not him, in accordance with what Allah had commanded him. He called the people who followed him to enter under his command and to obey him; and that is when he said, "Do not pour into it." So this man stopped what others had entered into, namely obedience to his foundation, by his refusal to enter the ark. Noah (peace be upon him) called him when he said: "O my son, ride with us, and do not be with the disbelievers," holding fast to the command — particularly with the longing to return to the beginning, in light of what he had previously seen from him of good obedience to his commands.

When Noah called him and he despaired of him entirely — that is, of the rank he had been hoping for — being hypocritical, arrogant, and refusing to obey based on what had happened, and Noah said that the command of Allah was upon him if he did not relinquish his presidency to him, otherwise it would be nullified — the opposite occurred with our guardian, peace be upon him. He admonished him at times and warned him at other times, saying: "The command of Allah is upon it, and if you do not yield to it, your presidency will go, and humiliation will overtake you. You will see no one who pretends to be your equal, nor any helper in your affairs" — which is what is meant by his saying: "And there is no preserver today from the command of Allah." When the son heard this from him, he showed disobedience and said: "He has no knowledge of this. This will not be done to you, that you should make the entire presidency in your house, even if it appears intentional, with reviling and abuse. I am supported by chiefs who have strengthened my hand and helped me to ward off humiliation from me" — which is what he meant by his saying: "I will take refuge in a mountain that will protect me from the water." The water here refers to that which divides itself against the force that destroys, and the mountain stands for what supports him of men and partisans. So he intended this and took up his case with his ilk, and they perished in his cycle, and there remained only those who held fast to obedience to his foundation. Allah has mentioned such news in His Noble Book as a warning to the community concerning what passes with the basic command from those who are intransigent and do not abide by it — sometimes through our Prophet's reference to it, O children of Adam; sometimes through the reference to the she-camel of Salih; and sometimes through the son of Noah — to make known that the conditions of Muhammad's cycle are like the conditions of
the aforementioned cycles. He did not assign Muhammad and his foundation, upon them be Allah's blessings, knowing the intransigence of their community,
— 0 211

<!-- page 214 -->
peace be upon them, and their language. This is a custom that has been carried out in the case of all the prophets and guardians, and so on until the time of the seventh. The retreat of the son of Noah was not to the latter, but rather to the people of the apparent who were in a similar state of hypocrisy. He sought their help, but "the sword of the uncle" was by the power of Allah, and Allah cleansed the earth of them. That is the flood that spread outwardly and inwardly. Likewise in the cycle of Muhammad, may Allah's prayers be upon him, some of it is what is right, some of it is true, and some of it is true — God willing. Only one who is reckoned among the people of the Alawi daʿwa knows of it. Allah is its light.
— 212

<!-- page 215 -->
Chapter Ten of the Book of Riyadh

On what is more sound, of his correction (islah), from the book of al-Mahsul, in the chapter of monotheism and creativity (al-ibdaʿ), which is the first thing in what was first to fix, of what he discussed and corrected.

Chapter One of Chapter Ten

We say:

The author of al-Mahsul, may Allah have mercy on him, did not exert himself, exaggerate, and apply his mind to the right of the daʿwa and its sons, nor to opening the doors of landmarks with what he made from the books of those in charge — he postponed it. And Sheikh Abu Hatim, may God have mercy on him, did not correct it, though he was able. To most people, this is from him: he stabbed at the author of al-Mahsul, then made apology for him, for his correction (al-islah) of that in his book; so he passed over it, and they reversed it — and that is a corrupt judgment. He has done something against the truth, and the matter is different from what they imagined. For the speaker (peace be upon him), when he knew, at the time of laying down things, that the sciences of religion are too many to encompass — that the imam should write them down in a single breath, or that you should memorize them in a single utterance — arranged them through many people without the imamate, in order that they should cooperate among themselves over all the sciences and their awareness, and memorize them, like the twelve hujjas (proofs), so that each of them benefits from those to whom Allah has granted the guidance of the righteous successors (al-aʾimma al-bararah), peace and blessings be upon them — the secret of things,
— 213

<!-- page 216 -->
their inner and outer aspects, according to their strength in receptivity and deduction, so that each may serve as a guide for others, just as the imams, peace be upon them, are in expression and benefit. They are like one person who gathers his parts together, and they are like the senses: each perceives things, and if one of them misses something which the other perceives, the perception of this second one is not a defect for the one who missed the perception, nor for the others.

If that is so, then the correction (islah) of Abu Hatim of what he corrected from the book of al-Mahsul is not, by Allah, a fault for him, nor for the author of al-Mahsul a deficiency. There is no challenge against either of them — except what we have said: that the people of the rank of correction in the sciences of religion are like the senses; if one of the senses misses to perceive something of the world of nature, the other does not miss it, but rather cooperates with it. The judgment of the truth is religion and the confirmation of the obligation owed to the Lord of the Worlds. Since that is so, I have seen in the book of al-Mahsul what was incumbent upon Abu Hatim, who was obligated to explain and correct, that he did not correct, and did not speak of, and which he ignored. So I had the right to cooperate in discharging the right of religion by stating what is implicated in what I have mentioned — what it is not permissible to believe regarding the chapter of monotheism and the first Creator (al-mubdiʿ al-awwal), without any other branches, may Allah help us. By the postponement of the term, we have already discussed it in other than this book, so it is not permissible for me to apologize for that, because the souls of religion are all one. If I apologize to myself — and Allah accepts from us that by which we draw near to Him from the guardianship which leads to His pleasure — may He be pleased with us, the Lord of the worlds, and gather us with the former, the reciprocal, the preceding, and the latecomer among our pure loyalists (mawali) in Dar al-Quds, a noble station.

Chapter Two of Chapter Ten

The author of al-Mahsul said:

In the chapter of monotheism: He is the creator of the thing — the rational thing, the illusory,
— 214

<!-- page 217 -->
the intellectual, the logical — I mean what is beneath these elements, and what is not beneath them.

We say:

It has been made necessary, by his saying this, that among the possessions of Allah Almighty which lie under His creativity is that which is not perceived by reason, illusion, or thought, and which is not spoken of by logic — and yet his existence is impossible, while believing in him is permissible. For whatever is not perceived by reason, illusion, or thought, and is not spoken of by logic, must, if it exists, either precede reason in its existence, or be with reason in its existence, or follow reason in its existence. It is impossible for it to precede reason, for reason is with the act, behind which is none but Allah Almighty, who has issued it and from whom it has come into being — and it is purely created (ibdaʿ), and the true existence (al-wujud al-haqq) which is the first existing thing from Allah Almighty. It is also impossible that its existence be one with the very intellect (1), for the intellect is the very intellect that is the creativity, and the intellect, when it occurs, is only one self and not two. Then, were its existence to be with the intellect — since they would be distinct and yet common in existence — it would follow that Allah Almighty had brought forth from Himself a multitude of creative causes, or that there is together with Him another Almighty, may He be exalted above that. Were the effect to exist in accordance with its cause, and yet the differing causes require two or more common causes, then the existence of each of them would be by reason of a proportion from them, distinct from the others — primarily. So it is impossible for distinct things to exist by one cause that has freed itself from the difference in proportions and additions. If its existence with the intellect requires this, then its existence is impossible — Allah is holy above all multiplicity, additions, and othernesses, and whatever becomes its cause. It is also impossible that its existence follow reason, for if its existence were after the intellect, then about it the minds would not be devoid of knowledge of it.
. (1) Omitted in copy (b).
— 215

<!-- page 218 -->
Nor would it be hard for them to define it; rather they would have known and defined it, just as they did all the other assets, sensible and intelligible, in the field of affirmation and negation. And since he was not devoid of three sections, each of which obliged that his existence be impossible, it is proven that his existence is impossible, and to say it is misguidance.

Chapter Three of Title Ten

Then, if the author of al-Mahsul does not say that the result of "the thing" is affirmative — that the thing is what Allah created, I mean what is under these elements and what is not under them — we would have said that by saying "the thing" he intended what was described as bodies, and as "nothing" except for the attributes of bodies from the world of creativity which are described in error by him who said so, believing in him. But when he mentioned what entails the affirmation of the impossible, it has only resulted in belief in the existence which Allah associates with in its purification, in a way that corruption spreads from every side — so we have shown that it is impossible.

Then we say:

"The thing" has come to be known as a common term under which fall all the assets of essences and accidents — sensible and intelligible — and it is not without intent in saying "nothing"; but rather what some of the wise men have said is that it is an affirmative for what is other than something, affirmatively stripped of what the thing is confined to in all its parts of essence and accidents, and elevated to the corrected state — and they have alluded to it.

The human being who is an affirmative for everything that is not human — the informer thereby strips us of existence, without affirming what is not for anything. They said: it is not the case that a letter intended not to be a letter has any reality removing it from existence, denying it that to which it is not by affirmation, which is another thing for him — like saying "the thing," which is the very thing from which falls everything that exists. If we meant by it "a cliff," no — we said "nothing" — and the very thing became vanished from what is in it.
— 216


<!-- page 219 -->
Without a proposition, it is distinct from him. And if he meant a partial eye within that eye — if he meant to make something positive and something else — then he said that God created him wrongly, because nothing is what has no attribute and does not exist. In the same way that it is an essence and an accident, the negation of the attributes of a thing was applied to God Almighty. He is purified and sanctified beyond them: the Almighty is neither an essence nor an accident, so these become attributes a thing has no attribute in, nor of, nor like — as though he said: the creator of the thing and of nothing is the creator of himself, who is other than the thing, and the creator of the thing is other than himself; and that is wrong, even if his intention was to negate the very thing.

His saying that Allah is the Creator of His Creator was wrong, for the thing is creativity, and it is the very eye of existence; and "nothing" is the negation of creativity, the nullification of existence. And if nothing is the negation of creativity, how can it be true that he is creative, when he has denied creativity from the impossible?

Chapter Four of Title X

The owner of the crop said:
The Creator of things is not of anything; only he and nothing with him — he is still he and nothing with him. We have denied the thing and the nothing, and we have made them all creative. We have denied every simple and complex image of who He is, and we have made everything from what happens. He must say, or not, that he is creative and that he is finite — nothing is after the thing, because the occurrence of its name only happened when the thing appeared.

We say:
It may be that the words "the Creator of things is sufficient for the sake of nothing," and the words "the Creator of things is nothing only, he and nothing with him," still involve what is not permissible to believe — namely that "nothing" is positive for what is not, in the eyes of the wise, over what we have already mentioned. So if he says "nothing with him," it is as if he said "it and what is not" — 217

<!-- page 220 -->
"with him, he is still," and that is shirk. Among the tongues that exist between human beings, there is no language able to express Allah in a manner appropriate to Him. The words and letters of the composite and the simple are all originated, and words, letters and languages are instruments by which humans understand each other regarding what is within themselves; they are originated, and they only indicate what was in the state of one's affairs. We have explained this in our treatise known as al-Riyāḍ.

He, the Almighty, is behind the minds and the perceptions, and behind a veil from understandings and thought, beyond which the paths of inquiry are cut off. When it becomes necessary to prove Him after knowing that all that is uttered (1) by the tongue, and by the movement of the lips with it, is a reality bearing upon what He has created and originated — the Almighty is not described by a word borrowed in its affirmative without proving an attribute or a plurality, except by a word that Allah has affirmed after exception: His saying, "Allah bears witness that there is no god but He," where He did not say "except Allah"; and likewise He said. Imam al-Muʿizz (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) indicated this in his well-known book. He said that "it" (huwa) is only Him, even if it is a borrowed word, for it is among the minds positive for what is outside of it, without any attribute or plurality.

The conduct of the path is established by the use of a letter that does not negate any kind of existence — more informed in the meaning of safety than the analogy, the disjunction, and the first — and it is true according to the scholars and jurists of the people of religion.

Chapter Five of Title X

He said:
And if we say that he and nothing with him, we have denied the thing and the nothing, and we have become naïve of all the prodigy. From where is it true that there is nothing that is said to be nothing, which falls under

(1) In copy (a) it is interrupted.
— 218

<!-- page 221 -->
creativity? And the existence of what is said to be nothing, which is ahead of creativity — which God has changed so that it is correct to deny it — it is nothing but the thing, and the thing is what we have denied.

We say: there is, in languages, what expresses Him because of the greatness of His importance, and the inadequacy of the originated letters in signifying, according to the one who is worthy of His grandeur. The "thing" that is good is other than Allah, who is the Finder, not from something that has an eye and a right to exist upon all its parts. "Nothing," then, is the negation of the eye of the thing, which is pure creativity, according to what he himself has said. And if nothing is the negation of the eye of creativity — which is the eye of existence and the truth of existence — how does it become creative in existence? These statements are not true.

Chapter Six of Title X

He said:
We have denied every simple and complex image of his identity, and we have made everything out of it. It is up to him to say or not to say that he is creative and is influenced by the truth.

We say:
The saying about which the findings were found, what does not fall upon him, Yasir Bag, all of them are creative — is that not a falsification?

Chapter Seven of Title X

He said:
Nothing after the thing, because the occurrence of its name is the appearance of something.

Nothing is not a name that falls upon an eye that has a share in existence; "the thing" is a name, and the one who is the letter of the pure has not been denied, and the negation of the name does not become a noun except for what the name has a name. It is not told about it except what the wise have mentioned: that — 219

<!-- page 222 -->
it involves the affirmation of something that has no name. The earlier words contain the answer to this, and it is sufficient.

Chapter Eight of Title X

The owner of the crop said:
In the first chapter of the creator, the Almighty created the world all at once. This is because he created the mind in one sentence, and in it the images of the two worlds emerged, and what is within them — without those images being referred to by their identities at the intellect. But the science of the mind is based on it, and it has information, except that the mind has already advanced upon it, either by act, but by force — it and the images all together.

We say:
This science — the mind that is said to have been created, and in which the images of the worlds and what is in them emerged — cannot be the First Intellect, that which exists from Allah, may He be exalted, first. For what is advanced in existence is dispensed with the perception of what is within it: its existence is related to its Creator who created it, and it does not need to know more than its knowledge of itself, that it is creative, and that its existence is not by itself but by another who is its Creator. It is the cause of the existence of what is below it, like the Imam who does not need to know others below him: he knows only that he is the cause of salvation without him, the mediator between those above him and those below him. But his rein is to know what is above him; and to know others who have advanced upon him to be in his presence — his rank requires that. Therefore it is necessary to delay him. And existence is to imagine all that it offers in existence, from the limits of acquisition, that survival and complete existence. If so, then what he mentioned is — 220

<!-- page 223 -->
the intellect that emanates from the natural world, not the First Intellect — supporting what we have said: it is the most prominent of the images of the worlds without (1) those images being indicated by their identities in the eyes of the intellect. But the world of the intellect is based on it, as he said: in power, he and all the images are together. So to say that is positive for what exists by force, and the news of what exists is not actually existing, nor does the First Mind exist.

Indeed, it is not permissible to say that there is something within it potent by force, because if it were so, it should be preceded by the type of its existence already existing in act, so that it brings it out into act — and this is invalidated by existing with the First Mind, or by something ahead of it. And if that is invalid, then it is not correct to say that the owner of the crop except in the late existence that has no other existence behind it. Its essence is with the knowledge of that which precedes it in existence from the two worlds; it is the second emanation from the world of nature, like the speaker who has the images of the worlds. The crop of these images has become already existing, and it has already been emitted.

Chapter Nine of Title Ten

The owner of the crop said:
When the mind's cause was the unity of the Almighty and the unity of eternity, the mind became eternal.

Based on that, we say:
He has made it obligatory by positing something that precedes the First Intellect in its existence — namely that cause which he called unity. And we have said that the intellect does not precede in its existence anything other than Allah, in the first place; so it is the first of eternity because of the impossibility of existing.

Loneliness is not a cause of reason, and it is other than it until it advances upon the intellect. Rather it is the intellect itself, and the intellect is the unity, which is the One.

(1) In copy (a) it is said.
— 221

<!-- page 224 -->
It is the cause; it is the effect; it is the creativity; it is the Creator; and it is the Perfect. The Perfect, which is the Eternal, the Eternal, the Existence, and the Essence — the One. The meanings these names require are worth adding to what His existence is — which is Allah, the Almighty — or by adding Him to what is below Him, or by adding it to itself, because the self is in its existence sufficient. This indicates what is said in this chapter about creativity.

The Creator is the same as the Creator, and his image is the image of the reasonable; if that is so, then also, when the unity was the same as the intellect, he said that the intellect became eternal. There is no eternity of its cause, for the intellect is nothing but the cause, so it becomes a cause eternal — but it is him, and he is it. Such an attribute, that I have made eternal, has no eternity of its cause. That is only true in the minds that emerge from the natural world, such as the Speakers (al-nuṭaqāʾ) and the Foundations (al-asās) and their followers, peace be upon them — whose minds are something, and by means of them they are humbled by something else, the reason that they are holy and eternal being that the eternal paradox of minds called the close angels extends their lights to them, and they unite with it.

The words of the owner of the crop, if they refer to the world of nature, are of the minds; not on the fate in the world of creativity. And if his words direct their meanings toward the minds in the abode of nature, then imagine that great limit and the rank in this capacity — it is impossible.

Chapter Ten of Chapter Ten

Then we say:
It is not without the meaning of what he said: that it is the cause of the very mind, but it is derived from it. The stream of the creator of the Almighty — he called it unity — is the one from which the stream of the monster flows,

(1) The sentence is completely omitted in year (a).
— 222

<!-- page 225 -->
or from it runs the course of the image from the body house, or from it runs the course of the purpose for which it was created (which is its eye and its self), and the role of the one who runs the course of his creator. Because unity, if it is a bug, the intellect has a thing, and the cause is a thing; and if the thing is not its existence by itself, then it is as if it is obligatory in Allah Almighty — whom He called the Unitarian — (originated) (1) after He was creative, by being based on others, in the sense that he has said it. And that is impossible.

Then, because unity is other than Allah, and that which is other than Allah was creative-originated, it has become obligatory that God, whom He called unity, be creative and originated; and this is impossible. It is invalid that it be the one from which the stream of the cytoplasm flows from existence, because it is impossible to exist a thing so that it exists in existence with God Almighty — so that He has something else with Him beyond what he said. He ceased being the one through whom the flow of the image from the assets in which it is found runs, because it is impossible for the image to exist only with that of which the course of matter is — and the existence of matter with God Almighty has been nullified, the presence of the image likewise. Glory be to Allah Almighty beyond the multiplication of images, which is the verse of the event, so that He becomes creative after being creative — Allah Almighty is Great above that.

It is invalid that it be the one from whom a stream of something is flowing for which it was created, because the mind was created not for the sake of unity; for if unity had what was created, it would not have existed. It has created a multitude, and it has found a multitude — so there is no unity if it exists. And when these aspects are invalidated, the meanings of saying that the cause of the unity of the mind is refrained from.

It has been proven that the eye of unity and the cause are the same, and its right; and if the mind is the eye of unity, the reason was that he said the mind became eternal for the eternity of its cause — even though what he meant by saying it, that first which is the First Being, is not true.

<!-- page 226 -->
Chapter Eleven of Title X

The author of *al-Maḥṣūl* said:

Since the form was made manifest in it from solitude, the form likewise became eternal for it, because the intellect became eternal in its entirety, not merely in part.

We say:

This is an attribute of something within whose power lies the image projected upon it; and it is not permissible to say this in accordance with the supreme limit which already exists, but only by force. And if it is so, then it is not correct to say what he said except in the case of the intellects which emerge from the intellects — such as the intellects of the prophets, the foundations, the imams and their followers, peace be upon them — who came forth into intellect through their own words. This is the paradoxical intellect called the proximate sovereign, nicknamed the Pen, in its entirety and timelessness. Their intellects, and the intellects of those who follow them upon the truth, attain this, and praise it by their speech.

The author of *al-Maḥṣūl* would not have said what he said had the forms not been creative in eternity; otherwise they would have no permanence, no return to the substrate of their origin from which they came forth with the form. They would have perished and vanished, and there would be no hope, no fear, no reward, no recompense, no punishment — for everything whose cause is eternal in it becomes eternal in it. If he says this, it implies that the said forms have no permanence and no connection with their substrates except by the eternal force, which is the one in the world of nature, derived from the souls which do not pass into action, and which gain permanence and continuance only for those who have attained eternity and perfection. Were it not for these, reward and punishment would be invalidated according to what he said. For the speaker and the imams, his position is correct because of this; so the meaning of what he said is not valid except in the intellects which emerge from the world of nature into the world of creation.

Chapter XII of Title X

The author of *al-Maḥṣūl* said:

And for us the intellect was made eternal by the eternity we have explained in the composite saying
- 224

<!-- page 227 -->
the Word of God, and there was no third intermediary between them, so the intellect became like it.

We say:

His saying leads to the meanings mentioned above, and is not worthy. It is not appropriate for the First Intellect, because it is an essence said to be identical with the Word — neither something else, nor something that was and then became like it. All this applies to the intellects which proceed from potency into act in the abode of nature, which become so by accepting the effects of the Word — that is, the First Intellect — and unite with it, as he confirms when he says: "For us, the form of action has become the form of the intellect."

The intellect is thus a cause of what is below it, and has become surrounded by the Word in what the Creator sees within Him. For he whose form has become the picture of it in the Word, and who has become a cause for what is below him, requires that he was not previously a cause and had no form in the Word — and such is the case with the intellects of the prophets, not the creative intellect without intermediary, which has never been other than the Word, nor is it the cause of being. Its existence is first and foremost — that without which the descriptions are broken off; it grows and is exalted.

We have spoken of this above concerning this supreme limit, and that is enough about prolonging the matter. Were it so, then the procedure of that supreme limit would be the course of these lower boundaries, which is impossible.

Chapter XIII of Title X

The author of *al-Maḥṣūl* said:

Since this is so, it is called creativity, because creativity is from the Creator; in complete creativity, only the perfect arises.

We say:

The Book of *al-Riyāḍ* [15]
- 225

<!-- page 228 -->
We have already said that his saying is mistaken in two respects. The first is that he called the intellect the creator and made it like its Creator, of whom he said it is perfect; this is shirk, and it is not permissible to say, because God is far above being identical in His essence to that which exists by His creative act. It is not said that the creative one with complete creativity is none but the perfect, so that the creativity may be complete. The second is that he applied the name of Creator to what belongs to the natural world, and that is impossible — because the one who deserves the name of creativity is the Being who is advanced over all things, not the thing which is itself created. If this is the case, then it is not permissible to believe what he said except in a way that is correct.

Chapter XIV of Title X

The author of *al-Maḥṣūl* said:

The intellect benefits images only from its cause, which is the Word — just as the two plates benefit from the sun's light, not from its body. And when it brings them forth, it does so from what is in it of the power of its cause, which is the Word; and this also benefited the intellect from it. Thus it became clear that the Word is what has become the cause of the things which emerge from the intellect, up to the very identity of the intellect; however, the intellect has become an intermediary between the Word and what is below it.

We say:

The intellect which he mentions is the intellects of the prophets and their followers, derived from their cause — which are others they quote — not the First Intellect, which is the First Creator. For the First Intellect does not need anything else in the existence of what exists through it, because it is the cause; and the particular Word in which and of which is the existence of what exists. Therefore we said that the Perfect proceeds from Him perfect and does not need anything outside
- 226

<!-- page 229 -->
itself, because it is the cause of the existence of things. If it were preceded by something else, then that something would be obliged to be the First Creator, not it — and this would lead to a disorder in the ranks of the principles, which is impossible. As for his saying that the intellect (1) has become an intermediary between the Word and what is below it, we have shown that this matter is impossible, as mentioned at the beginning of our book.

It is permissible to add and say:

How can anything precede the First Intellect, so as to be a means of action between Him and what is below? The intellect is identical with the Word, which is the cause that exists from God Almighty. And if it were permissible for something to precede it, that thing would not escape being either of the same kind as its existence — so its precedence over it would be invalid, and their ranks and limits would be equal, since they are of the same kind — though not of the same kind in its existence. Therefore, it is either something or nothing. If it is something, it is an object for the perception of intellects; and what the intellect perceives, the intellect is advanced over. So this cannot be. And if it is nothing, then it is not the Word, but it is transcendent above the qualities which a thing deserves in its parts — the Almighty is far exalted above this — in which case what should He be? And given the impossibility of anything being advanced over the First Intellect, there is nothing above the thing except the Thing of the Almighty. And if this is so, then it is the Word, it is the cause, it is the unity, and it is the intellect, according to what we have explained above. God is sufficient for us, and He is the best Trustee.

Chapter XV of Title X

(1) Dropped in copy (A).

The author of *al-Maḥṣūl* said:
- 227

<!-- page 230 -->
And creativity is an intermediary between the Creator and the created, the created being an effect of the influencer upon the influenced. He said: The form of creativity is intermediate between the doer and the object; its existence is on the side of the creative actor, while the effect of the form is found on the side of the created in the effect. This form — I mean creativity — has come to be in the Creator Almighty.

We say:

This speech contains an affirmation of that which God has not created, nor invented, nor originated. This is contrary to what monotheists are obligated to hold; for by saying that He made creativity uncreated, it is obligatory that creativity be a form in the Creator. Then by his saying, it is obligatory that the form which he called creation be a form, and that he called it an influencer in it — fixed, not invented, not originated.

It is not permissible to suppose that creativity is something other than creative; for if what he imagines as creative is other than creativity, then it must either be with God Almighty, or exist for itself. Its existence for itself is invalidated, for it would be fragmented in itself, while it is yet with God Almighty. As for its existence with God Almighty, this is not possible either, because its existence with God is not without being similar to God — glorified and exalted is He — and an example of Him, so that they would be two examples. These two would be affirmed by the competence of each in respect of the occurrence of duality, and by the competence in two things, which exist only for an affirmative cause — because they would be in that condition before them. Either their existence would be alike (and there is no likeness), or it would be that of two opposites — and the existence of two opposites occurs only in the presence of others who preserve their existence; for in the presence of one of the opposites is the invalidation of the existence of the other, because its existence is necessary. This would require that the Creator Almighty be created, and that what is primary be preceded — by the Almighty Himself — and that is more abstaining and more impossible. If there is something which necessitates its existence, it cannot be without two aspects: if the hero of all aspects is a hero whose existence is for itself; and if its existence for itself is invalidated, then it is proven that its existence is from
- 228

<!-- page 231 -->
God Almighty. And creativity has its existence from God Almighty, so the One is not one of creativity. And the creative One — to say that He is a creative or a primary creator from another — if that is so, then existence is invalidated, since the existing produces nothing but one. Thus it is proven that creativity is the Creator; and if creativity is the Creator, then what the author of *al-Maḥṣūl* said is wrong, so let him avoid it, God willing. And so we have come to what we were promised at the beginning of the book.

We say:

Tawḥīd and the knowledge of the limits are difficult, and yet they encompass the life and survival of souls, and their salvation from the world of nature and its impossibilities. Since it is difficult, and God Almighty knows that all His servants do not attain the degree by which they reach perfection in knowing the limits of God and His unity, He has from time to time singled out one man with perfection and election — such as the Imam, may God's prayers be upon him. By perfection I mean being complete in accepting the overflow taking place in the natural world from the side of the angels who are near to him; thus he will be dominant over them and will be promoted to His whole. God will make it obligatory upon them to obey him and to love him, that they may become a part of him, and that they may share in his compassion for them. There is no way to this except by adopting the two acts of worship and making good the truth from them in knowledge and action, both outwardly and inwardly, and being keen to preserve them. This is achieved only by remembering death and what follows from it — the paradox of parents, children, relatives, and homeland — and by the certainty that nothing brings one to the promised time except through surplus. And if there is no increase that is saved except by obedience, then its opportunities are fulfilled: the obligation that fulfills its right, good deeds, good actions that one performs, and knowledge of the realities of things. May God place us and the company of believers in the east of the earth
- 229

<!-- page 232 -->
and its west — those who conclude with goodness — and our provision and their intercession is the intercession of Muḥammad, ʿAlī, and the
(1) Dropped in copy (A).

pure nation, and our Imam [the Ruler by the Command of God] and his fathers, peace be upon them, in the land of Jerusalem with His mercy and mercy. Then we conclude the book with praise to God, Lord of the Worlds, and prayers upon the best of the first and the last, Muḥammad, the family of the Imams, and the rightly guiding Imams. And we say: there is no power but from God Almighty; what God wills. And I ask God for forgiveness, and I delegate my matter to God; God is sufficient for me — yes, the agent, yes the Lord, and yes the supporter. Praise be to God, until He is praised as is due; and prayers upon Muḥammad and his good family, all of them, the pure.

Subject Index

«Introduction to Development»
From page 5 to page 39

A brief presentation of the cultural mindset that dominated Islamic society in the late third century of the Hijra; of the doctrinal disputes and their causes; and of the influences that dominated writers and scholars in that early era. To what extent were the discussions and lectures taking their course? Among the noteworthy points is that the Ismāʿīliyya is considered one of the sects that contributed in great measure to these discussions — but on a larger scale and in a new and innovative field. The researcher acknowledges that intellectual liberation had a great impact on her beliefs, given that the debate was not limited to other ideologically hostile sects, but went beyond them to the Ismāʿīlī preachers themselves.

The first scientific discussion that took place at that time was the one in which each of the Ismāʿīlī preachers took part:
- 233

<!-- page 236 -->
Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad al-Nasafī, the author of the book *al-Maḥṣūl*; Abū Ḥātim al-Rāzī, the author of the book *al-Iṣlāḥ*; Abū Yaʿqūb al-Sijistānī, the author of the book *al-Nuṣra*; and Ḥamīd al-Dīn al-Kirmānī, the author of the book *al-Riyāḍ*. They dedicated these books to declaring their views on theology. The importance of the book *al-Riyāḍ* appeared in the scientific community when the traces of al-Kirmānī began to appear in existence; thus it is considered one of the rare books which represent the prevailing philosophical opinions in the third century AH and afterwards.

The introduction also contains the biography of al-Rāzī, his activity, his writings, and his opinions; then the biography of al-Sijistānī and his opinions; then the biography of Ḥamīd al-Dīn al-Kirmānī; and then the contents of the book *al-Riyāḍ*, its sections, and a quick and brief glimpse of the book, its chapters and sections.

«Author's Introduction»
From page 47 to page 52

A brief talk about the reasons that led him to write the book *al-Riyāḍ*, then a review of the views expressed in the three books *al-Maḥṣūl*, *al-Iṣlāḥ*, and *al-Nuṣra*, in summary form.

«Chapter One», from page 53 to page 100

Divided into thirty-eight chapters which examine the essence of the soul, which is the first issue.

«Chapter Two», from page 101 to page 110

Divided into nine chapters, examining the first chapter on the intellect, which is the First Creator.
- 234


<!-- page 237 -->

((Chapter Three)), from page 111 to page 118.
Divided into six chapters; examines the soul and the skeleton and whether they are similar to the First or not.

((Chapter Four)), from page 119 to page 126.
Divided into eight chapters; examines the contention that souls are parts and not traces.

((Chapter Five)), from page 127 to page 134.
Divided into seven chapters; argues that human beings are the fruit of the world.

((Chapter Six)), from page 135 to page 142.
Divided into nine chapters; examines movement, stillness, hysteria, and image.

((Chapter Seven)), from page 143 to page 152.
Divided into seven chapters; concerned with the sections of the world.

((Chapter Eight)), from page 153 to page 175.
Divided into twenty-four chapters on fate and destiny.

((Chapter Nine)), from page 176 to page 212.
Divided into thirty-three chapters; concerned with the chapter on the law of Adam and the guardian of the tablet.

((Chapter Ten)), from page 213 to page 230.
Divided into sixteen chapters; concerned with the chapter on Tawhid and the First Creator.

((French Introduction)) includes a definition of the Book of Riyad and the reason for its place.

<!-- page 253 -->

comparée entre celle-ci et les théories philosophiques officielles des ismaïlites.

Si la série d'ouvrages historiques et philosophiques déjà établis et publiés par nos soins s'enrichit aujourd'hui d'un volume nouveau, «ar-riad», cela ne saurait se faire sans un mot de reconnaissant hommage à l'éminent orientaliste qu'est Professeur W. Ivanow. Car c'est grâce à son infatigable initiative au service de la science que la plupart des manuscrits ismaéliens ont pu être mis à jour. Travail énorme et désintéressé qu'inspire un seul souci : celui d'informer le monde islamique sur cette philosophie universelle qui fit bouillonner les esprits pour un temps, fascina le regard des savants et fut, en Orient comme en Occident, à la fine pointe de leurs approximations.

Beyrouth — Liban
1960

— 251 —

Aref Tamer

<!-- page 254 -->

Le profit pour qui recherche l'origine de ces controverses, lorsqu'il s'applique à creuser les diverses opinions : il découvre que l'œuvre des auteurs de cette époque lointaine constitue un monument de science nouvelle par rapport à leur siècle, tant pour la pénétration des problèmes philosophiques que pour l'ampleur de la recherche dans le domaine des commentaires de textes et de l'exégèse des versets coraniques. Cet effort leur a valu d'approcher de la réalité et de s'en faire une conception raisonnée.

La plupart du temps les controverses en question avaient pour origine des discussions orales que se livraient les cercles et les centres d'études scientifiques. Elles prenaient la forme de longues conférences qui s'étalent dans les livres à longueur de pages. Parmi les groupements qui contribuaient abondamment à ces débats, nous trouvons celui des Ismaéliens. Mais ce qui est assez surprenant, c'est que, ces débats de théologie à peine terminés entre différentes sectes, nous voyons les Ismaéliens s'engager dans un autre genre de controverse, un genre tout nouveau... C'est la controverse entre leurs Da'is eux-mêmes. Ceci prouve clairement que la liberté de pensée était chez eux une loi souveraine. Le dynamisme de leur réflexion intellectuelle, affranchie des chaînes de la tradition, s'imposait ainsi aux milieux conservateurs et les forçait à l'abandon des positions surannées.

L'ouvrage intitulé «al-mahsul» parut dans les milieux ismaéliens au début du 4ème siècle de l'Hégire (10ème siècle après Jésus-Christ). Il est attribué au Da'i an-Nasafi ; il est curieux qu'al-Kirmani, en parlant de ce texte, omette de mentionner son auteur. Peut-être cette omission est-elle un indice que le livre a été attribué par erreur à an-Nasafi. La faveur obtenue par «al-mahsul» dans les milieux ismaéliens amena le Da'i Abu Hatim ar-Razi à rédiger de son côté un écrit intitulé «al-islah». Ce livre renferme une critique de certaines opinions rapportées par «al-mahsul». Cette discussion poussa un autre grand Da'i, Abu Ya'qub as-Sijistani, à intervenir à son tour contre ce qu'il estimait contraire à la vérité et aux principes philosophiques. Dans son livre «an-nasra» il prit le parti de l'auteur d'«al-mahsul» et critiqua ar-Razi sans toutefois chercher à ruiner la position de celui-ci.

Peu de temps après lui, al-Kirmani aborda le même sujet de façon magistrale. Ce fut dans ce précieux traité «ar-riad» : il se donna le rôle d'arbitre entre les auteurs d'«al-islah» et d'«an-nasra» et sut, avec une habileté consommée, à la fois combler d'éloges et critiquer avec rigueur scientifique les différentes positions des trois livres, en les confrontant avec la doctrine fondamentale de l'Ismaélisme. Autrement dit, son ouvrage constitue une étude

— 252 —


<!-- page 255 -->

The book we present today to the experts of the philosophical sciences is called *ar-Riyad*. Its author is Sayyidna Hamid ad-Din Ahmad b. Abdallah al-Kirmani, who was Da'i of the Fatimid Imam, the caliph al-Hakim bi-Amrillah, in Iraq and Persia. He bore the title *Hujjat al-'Iraqain* (charged with the Ismaili mission for these two regions).

The Ismaili religious leaders count *ar-Riyad* among the important works addressed to the most learned of those who occupy the first ranks of the sect. It is therefore characterized by the elevated level and the force of its doctrine. This explains why beginners in philosophical research have found it difficult to understand the implications of this text and to penetrate the nuances of its technical vocabulary.

*Ar-Riyad* marks a stage in the evolution of Islamic thought and presents us with a clear image of the growth of the Ismaili doctrinal edifice. And once we know that the book sets out in condensed form the dominant teaching of this period of Ismailism, we understand the influence it was able to exercise. There are good reasons to regard this text as a general philosophical conference worked out by four of the great Ismaili Da'is of the early period, into which they inserted their efforts of philosophical reflection as well as their esoteric exegesis. They are: the Da'i Muhammad b. Ahmad an-Nasafi, Abu Hatim ar-Razi, Abu Ya'qub as-Sijistani, and Hamid ad-Din al-Kirmani. In this joint critical work the four thinkers devoted themselves passionately to the defense of their speculation and condensed their doctrine within it.

4

It is acknowledged today that toward the end of the 3rd century of the Hijra the Islamic world displayed the features of an advanced state of culture—scientific, philosophical, and literary—but stirred by new movements and varied doctrinal controversies. The theologians at that time engaged in endless debates, freed from any fixed mode of expression. How great, then, must be
